<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">

<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p><i><b>Avatar</b></i> (marketed as <i><b>James Cameron's Avatar</b></i>) is a 2009 American<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Epic_film" title="Epic film">epic</a> <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction_film" title="Science fiction film">science fiction film</a> directed, written, co-produced, and co-edited by <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron" title="James Cameron">James Cameron</a>, and starring <a href="/wiki/Sam_Worthington" title="Sam Worthington">Sam Worthington</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoe_Saldana" title="Zoe Saldana">Zoe Saldana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Lang" title="Stephen Lang">Stephen Lang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Rodriguez" title="Michelle Rodriguez">Michelle Rodriguez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Ribisi" title="Giovanni Ribisi">Giovanni Ribisi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sigourney_Weaver" title="Sigourney Weaver">Sigourney Weaver</a>. The film is set in the mid-22nd century, when humans are mining a <a href="/wiki/Room-temperature_superconductor" title="Room-temperature superconductor">room-temperature superconductor</a> called <a href="/wiki/Unobtainium" title="Unobtainium">unobtanium</a> on <a href="/wiki/Fictional_universe_of_Avatar#Astronomy_and_geology" title="Fictional universe of Avatar">Pandora</a>, a lush <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habitable_moon" title="Habitable moon">habitable moon</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Gas_giant" title="Gas giant">gas giant</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Centauri" title="Alpha Centauri">Alpha Centauri</a> star system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horwitz2009_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Horwitz2009-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> The expansion of the mining colony threatens the continued existence of a local tribe of <a href="/wiki/Pandoran_biosphere#Na.CA.BCvi" title="Pandoran biosphere">Na'vi</a> – a <a href="/wiki/Humanoid" title="Humanoid">humanoid</a> species indigenous to Pandora. The film's title refers to a <a href="/wiki/Genetic_engineering" title="Genetic engineering">genetically engineered</a> Na'vi body with the mind of a remotely located human that is used to interact with the natives of Pandora.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Time-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Development of <i>Avatar</i> began in 1994, when Cameron wrote an 80-page treatment for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QA_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-QA-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-abc-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> Filming was supposed to take place after the completion of Cameron's 1997 film <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i>, for a planned release in 1999,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> but according to Cameron, the necessary technology was not yet available to achieve his vision of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1996_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1996-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> Work on <a href="/wiki/Na%27vi_language" title="Na'vi language">the language</a> of the film's <a href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_life" title="Extraterrestrial life">extraterrestrial beings</a> began in 2005, and Cameron began developing the screenplay and <a href="/wiki/Fictional_universe_of_Avatar" title="Fictional universe of Avatar">fictional universe</a> in early 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-USCMarshall_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-USCMarshall-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radionz1_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-radionz1-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Avatar</i> was officially budgeted at $237 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Patten_.282009.29_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Patten_.282009.29-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Other estimates put the cost between $280 million and $310 million for production and at $150 million for promotion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.nytimes.com_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.nytimes.com-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_budget_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimes_budget-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vanityfair_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-vanityfair-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The film made extensive use of new <a href="/wiki/Motion_capture" title="Motion capture">motion capture</a> filming techniques,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PM_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-PM-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> and was released for traditional viewing, <a href="/wiki/3D_film" title="3D film">3D</a> viewing (using the <a href="/wiki/RealD_3D" title="RealD 3D">RealD 3D</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dolby_3D" title="Dolby 3D">Dolby 3D</a>, <a href="/wiki/XpanD_3D" title="XpanD 3D">XpanD 3D</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IMAX_3D" title="IMAX 3D">IMAX 3D</a> formats), and for "<a href="/wiki/4D_film" title="4D film">4D</a>" experiences in select South Korean theaters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4-D_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-4-D-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Stereoscopy" title="Stereoscopy">stereoscopic</a> filmmaking was touted as a breakthrough in cinematic technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Avatar</i> premiered in London on <span class="nowrap">December 10</span>, 2009, and was internationally released on <span class="nowrap">December 16</span> and in the United States and Canada on <span class="nowrap">December 18</span>, to positive critical reviews, with critics highly praising its groundbreaking visual effects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-D_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-D-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.comingsoon.net_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.comingsoon.net-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.reuters.com_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.reuters.com-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> During its theatrical run, the film broke several box office records and became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">highest-grossing film of all time</a>, as well as in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">United States and Canada</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> surpassing <i>Titanic</i>, which had held those records for twelve years (and was also directed by Cameron).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxofficemojoalltime_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxofficemojoalltime-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> It also became the first film to gross more than <span class="nowrap">$2 billion</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Avatar</i> was nominated for nine <a href="/wiki/82nd_Academy_Awards" title="82nd Academy Awards">Academy Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Best Picture</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Academy Award for Best Director">Best Director</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-List_of_Academy_Award_nominations_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-List_of_Academy_Award_nominations-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> and won three, for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Art_Direction" title="Academy Award for Best Art Direction">Best Art Direction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Cinematography" title="Academy Award for Best Cinematography">Best Cinematography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects" title="Academy Award for Best Visual Effects">Best Visual Effects</a>. Following the film's success, Cameron signed with <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a> to produce three sequels, making <i>Avatar</i> the first of a planned tetralogy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> The three sequels, all directed and co-written by Cameron, will be released each year starting from December 2017 to 2019.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span></h2>
<p>By 2154, humans have severely depleted <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a>'s natural resources, leading to a severe energy crisis. The Resources Development Administration (RDA) mines for a valuable mineral – <a href="/wiki/Unobtainium" title="Unobtainium">unobtanium</a> – on Pandora, a densely forested <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habitable_moon" title="Habitable moon">habitable moon</a> orbiting the <a href="/wiki/Gas_giant" title="Gas giant">gas giant</a> Polyphemus in the <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Centauri" title="Alpha Centauri">Alpha Centauri</a> star system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Horwitz2009_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Horwitz2009-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Pandora, whose atmosphere is poisonous to humans, is inhabited by the <a href="/wiki/Pandoran_biosphere#Na.CA.BCvi" title="Pandoran biosphere">Na'vi</a>, 10-foot tall (3.0 m), blue-skinned, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sapience" title="Sapience">sapient</a> humanoids<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> who live in harmony with nature and worship a <a href="/wiki/Mother_goddess" title="Mother goddess">mother goddess</a> called Eywa.</p>
<p>To explore Pandora's <a href="/wiki/Biosphere" title="Biosphere">biosphere</a>, scientists use Na'vi-human hybrids called "avatars", operated by genetically matched humans; Jake Sully, a paraplegic former <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Marine" title="United States Marine">Marine</a>, replaces his deceased twin brother as an operator of one. Dr. Grace Augustine, head of the Avatar Program, considers Sully an inadequate replacement but accepts his assignment as a bodyguard. While protecting the avatars of Grace and scientist Norm Spellman as they collect biological data, Jake's avatar is attacked by a <a href="/wiki/Pandoran_biosphere#Fauna" title="Pandoran biosphere">thanator</a> and flees into the forest, where he is rescued by Neytiri, a female Na'vi. Witnessing an auspicious sign, she takes him to her clan, whereupon Neytiri's mother Mo'at, the clan's spiritual leader, orders her daughter to initiate Jake into their society.</p>
<p>Colonel Miles Quaritch, head of RDA's <a href="/wiki/Private_military_company" title="Private military company">private security force</a>, promises Jake that the company will restore his legs if he gathers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intelligence_(information_gathering)" title="Intelligence (information gathering)">intelligence</a> about the Na'vi and the clan's gathering place, a giant arboreal called Hometree,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Script25_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-Script25-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> on grounds that it stands above the richest deposit of unobtanium in the area. When Grace learns of this, she transfers herself, Jake, and Norm to an <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/outpost" title="wikt:outpost">outpost</a>. Over three months, Jake grows to sympathize with the natives. After Jake is initiated into the tribe, he and Neytiri choose each other as mates, and soon afterward, Jake reveals his change of allegiance when he attempts to disable a bulldozer that threatens to destroy a sacred Na'vi site. When Quaritch shows a video recording of Jake's attack on the bulldozer to Administrator Parker Selfridge,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Script8and15_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Script8and15-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> and another in which Jake admits that the Na'vi will never abandon Hometree, Selfridge orders Hometree destroyed.</p>
<p>Despite Grace's argument that destroying Hometree could damage the <a href="/wiki/Biological_neural_network" title="Biological neural network">biological neural network</a> native to Pandora, Selfridge gives Jake and Grace one hour to convince the Na'vi to evacuate before commencing the attack. While trying to warn the Na'vi, Jake confesses to being a spy and the Na'vi take him and Grace captive. Seeing this, Quaritch's men destroy Hometree, killing Neytiri's father (the clan chief) and many others. Mo'at frees Jake and Grace, but they are detached from their avatars and imprisoned by Quaritch's forces. Pilot Trudy Chacón, disgusted by Quaritch's brutality, carries them to Grace's outpost, but during the escape, Quaritch fires at them, hitting Grace.</p>
<p>To regain the Na'vi's trust, Jake connects his mind to that of Toruk, a dragon-like predator feared and honored by the Na'vi. Jake finds the refugees at the sacred <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fictional_universe_in_Avatar#The_Tree_of_Souls" title="Fictional universe in Avatar">Tree of Souls</a> and pleads with Mo'at to heal Grace. The clan attempts to transfer Grace from her human body into her avatar with the aid of the Tree of Souls, but she dies before the process can complete.</p>
<p>Supported by the new chief Tsu'tey, who acts as Jake's translator, Jake speaks to unite the clan and tells them to gather all of the clans to battle against the RDA. Noticing the impending gathering, Quaritch organizes a <a href="/wiki/Preemptive_war" title="Preemptive war">pre-emptive strike</a> against the Tree of Souls, believing that its destruction will demoralize the natives. On the eve of battle, Jake prays to Eywa, via a neural connection to the Tree of Souls, to intercede on behalf of the Na'vi.</p>
<p>During the subsequent battle, the Na'vi suffer heavy casualties, including Tsu'tey and Trudy; but are rescued when <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Characters_and_wildlife_in_Avatar#Fauna" title="Characters and wildlife in Avatar">Pandoran wildlife</a> unexpectedly join the attack and overwhelm the humans, which Neytiri interprets as Eywa's answer to Jake's prayer. Then Jake destroys a makeshift bomber before it can reach the Tree of Souls; Quaritch escapes from his own damaged aircraft, wearing an <a href="/wiki/Mecha" title="Mecha">AMP suit</a> and breaks open the avatar link unit containing Jake's human body, exposing it to Pandora's poisonous atmosphere. Quaritch then prepares to slit the throat of Jake's avatar, but Neytiri kills Quaritch and saves Jake from suffocation.</p>
<p>With the exceptions of Jake, Norm, Max (another scientist), and a select few others, all humans are expelled from Pandora and sent back to Earth, after which Jake is transferred permanently into his avatar with the aid of the Tree of Souls.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Fictional_universe_of_Avatar" title="Fictional universe of Avatar">Fictional universe of Avatar</a></div>
<dl>
<dt>Humans</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><span id="Worthington"></span><a href="/wiki/Sam_Worthington" title="Sam Worthington">Sam Worthington</a> as Jake Sully, a <a href="/wiki/Disability" title="Disability">disabled</a> former Marine who becomes part of the Avatar Program after his twin brother is killed. His military background helps the Na'vi warriors relate to him. Cameron cast the Australian actor after a worldwide search for promising young actors, preferring relative unknowns to keep the budget down.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> Worthington, who was living in his car at the time,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> auditioned twice early in development,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QA2_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-QA2-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> and he has signed on for possible sequels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron felt that because Worthington had not done a major film, he would give the character "a quality that is really real". Cameron said he "has that quality of being a guy you'd want to have a beer with, and he ultimately becomes a leader who transforms the world".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Lang" title="Stephen Lang">Stephen Lang</a> as Colonel Miles Quaritch, the head of the mining operation's security detail. Fiercely loyal to his military code, he has a profound disregard for Pandora's inhabitants that is evident in both his actions and his language. Lang had unsuccessfully auditioned for a role in Cameron's <i><a href="/wiki/Aliens_(film)" title="Aliens (film)">Aliens</a></i> (1986), but the director remembered Lang and sought him for <i>Avatar</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lang_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-lang-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Biehn" title="Michael Biehn">Michael Biehn</a>, who <i>was</i> in <i>Aliens</i>, read the script and watched some of the 3-D footage with Cameron,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> but was ultimately not cast in the role.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sigourney_Weaver" title="Sigourney Weaver">Sigourney Weaver</a> as Dr. Grace Augustine, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Astrobiologist" title="Astrobiologist">exobiologist</a> and head of the Avatar Program. She is also Sully's mentor and an advocate of peaceful relations with the Na'vi, having set up a school to teach them English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michelle_Rodriguez" title="Michelle Rodriguez">Michelle Rodriguez</a> as Trudy Chacón, a combat pilot assigned to support the Avatar Program who is sympathetic to the Na'vi. Cameron had wanted to work with Rodriguez since seeing her in <i><a href="/wiki/Girlfight" title="Girlfight">Girlfight</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lang_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-lang-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Ribisi" title="Giovanni Ribisi">Giovanni Ribisi</a> as Parker Selfridge, the corporate administrator for the RDA mining operation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> While he is at first willing to destroy the Na'vi civilization to preserve the company's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bottom_line" title="Bottom line">bottom line</a>, he is reluctant to authorize the attacks on the Na'vi and taint his image, doing so only after Quaritch persuades him that it is necessary, and the attacks will be humane. When the attacks are broadcast to the base, Selfridge displays discomfort at the violence.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joel_David_Moore" title="Joel David Moore">Joel David Moore</a> as Dr. Norm Spellman, a xenoanthropologist<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cameron2007P10_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cameron2007P10-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> who studies plant and animal life as part of the Avatar Program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lux2009_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lux2009-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> He arrives on Pandora at the same time as Sully and operates an avatar. Although he is expected to lead the diplomatic contact with the Na'vi, it turns out that Jake has the personality better suited to win the natives' respect.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dileep_Rao" title="Dileep Rao">Dileep Rao</a> as Dr. Max Patel, a scientist who works in the Avatar Program and comes to support Jake's rebellion against the RDA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<dl>
<dt>Na'vi</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li><span id="Saldana"></span><a href="/wiki/Zoe_Saldana" title="Zoe Saldana">Zoe Saldana</a> as Neytiri, the daughter of the leader of the Omaticaya (the Na'vi clan central to the story). She is attracted to Jake because of his bravery, though frustrated with him for what she sees as his naiveté and stupidity. She serves as Jake's love interest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brennan2007_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brennan2007-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> The character, like all the Na'vi, was created using <a href="/wiki/Motion_capture" title="Motion capture">performance capture</a>, and its visual aspect is entirely computer generated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Saldana has also signed on for potential sequels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-starts_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-starts-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/C._C._H._Pounder" title="C. C. H. Pounder">C. C. H. Pounder</a> as Mo'at, the Omaticaya's spiritual leader, Neytiri's mother, and consort to clan leader Eytukan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wes_Studi" title="Wes Studi">Wes Studi</a> as Eytukan, the Omaticaya's clan leader, Neytiri's father, and Mo'at's mate.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Laz_Alonso" title="Laz Alonso">Laz Alonso</a> as Tsu'tey, the finest warrior of the Omaticaya. He is heir to the chieftainship of the tribe. At the beginning of the film's story, he is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Betrothal" title="Betrothal">betrothed</a> to Neytiri.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span></h3>
<p>In 1994,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abc_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-abc-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> director James Cameron wrote an 80-page <a href="/wiki/Film_treatment" title="Film treatment">treatment</a> for <i>Avatar</i>, drawing inspiration from "every single science fiction book" he had read in his childhood as well as from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adventure_novel" title="Adventure novel">adventure novels</a> by <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Rice_Burroughs" title="Edgar Rice Burroughs">Edgar Rice Burroughs</a> and <a href="/wiki/H._Rider_Haggard" title="H. Rider Haggard">H. Rider Haggard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QA_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-QA-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> In <span class="nowrap">August 1996</span>, Cameron announced that after completing <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i>, he would film <i>Avatar</i>, which would make use of synthetic, or <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated</a>, actors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1996_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1996-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The project would cost $100 million and involve at least six actors in leading roles "who appear to be real but do not exist in the physical world".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup> Visual effects house <a href="/wiki/Digital_Domain" title="Digital Domain">Digital Domain</a>, with whom Cameron has a partnership, joined the project, which was supposed to begin production in mid-1997 for a 1999 release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> However, Cameron felt that the technology had not caught up with the story and vision that he intended to tell. He decided to concentrate on making documentaries and refining the technology for the next few years. It was revealed in a <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bloomberg_BusinessWeek" title="Bloomberg BusinessWeek">Bloomberg BusinessWeek</a></i> cover story that 20th Century Fox had fronted $10 million to Cameron to film a proof-of-concept clip for <i>Avatar</i>, which he showed to Fox executives in <span class="nowrap">October 2005</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessweek_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-businessweek-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2006, Cameron revealed that his film <i>Project 880</i> was "a retooled version of <i>Avatar</i>", a film that he had tried to make years earlier,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> citing the technological advances in the creation of the computer-generated characters <a href="/wiki/Gollum" title="Gollum">Gollum</a>, <a href="/wiki/King_Kong_(2005_film)" title="King Kong (2005 film)">King Kong</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Davy_Jones_(Pirates_of_the_Caribbean)" title="Davy Jones (Pirates of the Caribbean)">Davy Jones</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QA_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-QA-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron had chosen <i>Avatar</i> over his project <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_Angel#Film" title="Battle Angel">Battle Angel</a></i> after completing a five-day camera test in the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small plainlinks" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><img alt="" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="759" height="22" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/40px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/60px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Wikinews-logo.svg/80px-Wikinews-logo.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">Wikinews has related news: <i><b><a class="extiw" href="//en.wikinews.org/wiki/Elvish,_Klingon_and_Na%27vi:_Constructed_languages_gain_foothold_in_film" title="wikinews:Elvish, Klingon and Na'vi: Constructed languages gain foothold in film">Elvish, Klingon and Na'vi: Constructed languages gain foothold in film</a></b></i></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>From January to April 2006, Cameron worked on the script and developed a culture for the film's aliens, the Na'vi. Their <a href="/wiki/Na%27vi_language" title="Na'vi language">language</a> was created by Dr. <a href="/wiki/Paul_Frommer" title="Paul Frommer">Paul Frommer</a>, a linguist at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">USC</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QA_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-QA-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The Na'vi language has a lexicon of about 1000 words, with some 30 added by Cameron. The tongue's <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phonemes</a> include <a href="/wiki/Ejective_consonant" title="Ejective consonant">ejective consonants</a> (such as the "kx" in "skxawng") that are found in the <a href="/wiki/Amharic" title="Amharic">Amharic</a> language of <a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a>, and the initial "ng" that Cameron may have taken from New Zealand <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_language" title="Māori language">Māori</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-radionz1_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-radionz1-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> Actress Sigourney Weaver and the film's <a href="/wiki/Scenic_design" title="Scenic design">set designers</a> met with Jodie S. Holt, professor of <a href="/wiki/Plant_physiology" title="Plant physiology">plant physiology</a> at <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Riverside" title="University of California, Riverside">University of California, Riverside</a>, to learn about the methods used by <a href="/wiki/Botany" title="Botany">botanists</a> to study and sample plants, and to discuss ways to explain the communication between Pandora's organisms depicted in the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>From 2005 to 2007, Cameron worked with a handful of designers, including famed fantasy illustrator <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Barlowe" title="Wayne Barlowe">Wayne Barlowe</a> and renowned concept artist <a href="/wiki/Jordu_Schell" title="Jordu Schell">Jordu Schell</a>, to shape the design of the Na'vi with paintings and physical sculptures when Cameron felt that 3-D brush renderings were not capturing his vision,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> often working together in the kitchen of Cameron's <a href="/wiki/Malibu,_California" title="Malibu, California">Malibu</a> home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> In <span class="nowrap">July 2006</span>, Cameron announced that he would film <i>Avatar</i> for a mid-2008 release and planned to begin principal photography with an established cast by <span class="nowrap">February 2007</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extravaganza_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-extravaganza-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The following August, the visual effects studio <a href="/wiki/Weta_Digital" title="Weta Digital">Weta Digital</a> signed on to help Cameron produce <i>Avatar</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stan_Winston" title="Stan Winston">Stan Winston</a>, who had collaborated with Cameron in the past, joined <i>Avatar</i> to help with the film's designs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Production_design" title="Production design">Production design</a> for the film took several years. The film had two different production designers, and two separate art departments, one of which focused on the <a href="/wiki/Flora" title="Flora">flora</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fauna" title="Fauna">fauna</a> of Pandora, and another that created human machines and human factors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-io9jamsession_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-io9jamsession-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> In <span class="nowrap">September 2006</span>, Cameron was announced to be using his own <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_cinematography_cameras#Fusion_Camera_System" title="Digital cinematography cameras">Reality Camera System</a> to film in 3-D. The system would use two high-definition cameras in a single camera body to create depth perception.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Fox was wavering because of its painful experience with cost overruns and delays on Cameron's previous picture, <i>Titanic</i>, even though Cameron rewrote <i>Avatar's</i> script to combine several characters together and offered to cut his fee in case the film flopped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessweek_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-businessweek-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron installed a traffic light with the amber signal lit outside of co-producer <a href="/wiki/Jon_Landau_(film_producer)" title="Jon Landau (film producer)">Jon Landau</a>'s office to represent the film's uncertain future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessweek_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-businessweek-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> In mid-2006, Fox told Cameron "in no uncertain terms that they were passing on this film," so he began shopping it around to other studios, and showed his proof-of-concept to <a href="/wiki/Dick_Cook" title="Dick Cook">Dick Cook</a> (then chairman of the <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Studios_(division)" title="The Walt Disney Studios (division)">Walt Disney Studios</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessweek_55-3"><a href="#cite_note-businessweek-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> However, when <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Pictures" title="Walt Disney Pictures">Disney</a> attempted to take over, Fox exercised its <a href="/wiki/Right_of_first_refusal" title="Right of first refusal">right of first refusal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessweek_55-4"><a href="#cite_note-businessweek-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> In <span class="nowrap">October 2006</span>, Fox finally agreed to commit to making <i>Avatar</i> after Ingenious Media agreed to back the film, which reduced Fox's financial exposure to less than half of the film's official $237 million budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-businessweek_55-5"><a href="#cite_note-businessweek-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> After Fox accepted <i>Avatar</i>, one skeptical Fox executive shook his head and told Cameron and Landau, "I don't know if we're crazier for letting you do this, or if you're crazier for thinking you <i>can</i> do this ..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;float: right; clear: right; margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em">
<caption>External audio</caption>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-style: italic">James Cameron interviewed by <a href="/wiki/F._X._Feeney" title="F. X. Feeney">F. X. Feeney</a> on writing Avatar.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align: left"><img alt="" data-file-height="128" data-file-width="128" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Nuvola_apps_arts.svg/16px-Nuvola_apps_arts.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Nuvola_apps_arts.svg/24px-Nuvola_apps_arts.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Nuvola_apps_arts.svg/32px-Nuvola_apps_arts.svg.png 2x" width="16"/> <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110728174551/http://media.wgaw.org/audio/Cameron_Feeney.mp3" rel="nofollow">Interview</a>, from here<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In December 2006, Cameron described <i>Avatar</i> as "a futuristic tale set on a planet 200 years hence ... an old-fashioned jungle adventure with an environmental conscience [that] aspires to a mythic level of storytelling".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-king_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-king-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> The <span class="nowrap">January 2007</span> press release described the film as "an emotional journey of redemption and revolution" and said the story is of "a wounded former Marine, thrust unwillingly into an effort to settle and exploit an exotic planet rich in <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biodiversity</a>, who eventually crosses over to lead the indigenous race in a battle for survival". The story would be of an entire world complete with an ecosystem of <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/phantasmagoria" title="wikt:phantasmagoria">phantasmagorical</a> plants and creatures, and native people with a rich culture and language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-starts_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-starts-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Estimates put the cost of the film at about $280–310 million to produce and an estimated $150 million for marketing, noting that about $30 million in <a href="/wiki/Tax_credit" title="Tax credit">tax credits</a> will lessen the financial impact on the studio and its financiers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.nytimes.com_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-www.nytimes.com-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_budget_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-latimes_budget-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vanityfair_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-vanityfair-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> A studio spokesperson said that the budget was "$237 million, with $150 million for promotion, end of story."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Patten_.282009.29_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Patten_.282009.29-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Themes_and_inspirations">Themes and inspirations</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Themes_in_Avatar" title="Themes in Avatar">Themes in Avatar</a></div>
<p><i>Avatar</i> is primarily an action-adventure journey of self-discovery, in the context of <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperialism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deep_ecology" title="Deep ecology">deep ecology</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-themes_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-themes-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron said his inspiration was "every single science fiction book I read as a kid", and that he was particularly striving to update the style of <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Rice_Burroughs" title="Edgar Rice Burroughs">Edgar Rice Burroughs's</a> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Carter_(character)" title="John Carter (character)">John Carter</a></i> series and the deep jungles of Pandora were visualized from Disney's 37th animated film, <i><a href="/wiki/Tarzan_(1999_film)" title="Tarzan (1999 film)">Tarzan</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-QA2_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-QA2-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> He acknowledged that <i>Avatar</i> shares themes with the films <i><a href="/wiki/At_Play_in_the_Fields_of_the_Lord" title="At Play in the Fields of the Lord">At Play in the Fields of the Lord</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Emerald_Forest" title="The Emerald Forest">The Emerald Forest</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Princess_Mononoke" title="Princess Mononoke">Princess Mononoke</a></i>, which feature clashes between cultures and civilizations, and with <i><a href="/wiki/Dances_with_Wolves" title="Dances with Wolves">Dances with Wolves</a>,</i> where a battered soldier finds himself drawn to the culture he was initially fighting against.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimesblogs.latimes.com_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimesblogs.latimes.com-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sankei_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-sankei-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a 2007 interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> magazine, Cameron was asked about the meaning of the term <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar" title="Avatar">Avatar</a></i>, to which he replied, "It's an incarnation of one of the <a href="/wiki/Hindu_deities" title="Hindu deities">Hindu gods</a> taking a flesh form. In this film what that means is that the human technology in the future is capable of injecting a human's intelligence into a remotely located body, a biological body."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Time-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Avatarjakeneytiri.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="281" data-file-width="500" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/38/Avatarjakeneytiri.jpg/220px-Avatarjakeneytiri.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/38/Avatarjakeneytiri.jpg/330px-Avatarjakeneytiri.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/38/Avatarjakeneytiri.jpg/440px-Avatarjakeneytiri.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Avatarjakeneytiri.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jake's avatar and Neytiri. One of the inspirations for the look of the Na'vi came from a dream that Cameron's mother had told him about.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-themes_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-themes-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The look of the Na'vi – the humanoids indigenous to Pandora – was inspired by a dream that Cameron's mother had, long before he started work on <i>Avatar</i>. In her dream, she saw a blue-skinned woman 12 feet (<span class="nowrap">4 m</span>) tall, which he thought was "kind of a cool image".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-themes_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-themes-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> Also he said, "I just like blue. It's a good color ... plus, there's a connection to the Hindu deities,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> which I like conceptually."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew.comQ1_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-ew.comQ1-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> He included similar creatures in his first screenplay (written in 1976 or 1977), which featured a planet with a native population of "gorgeous" tall blue aliens. The Na'vi were based on them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-themes_69-3"><a href="#cite_note-themes-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>For the love story between characters Jake and Neytiri, Cameron applied a <a href="/wiki/Star-crossed" title="Star-crossed">star-crossed</a> love theme, and acknowledged its similarity to the pairing of Jack and Rose from his film <i>Titanic.</i> An interviewer stated, "Both couples come from radically different cultures that are contemptuous of their relationship and are forced to choose sides between the competing communities."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.MTV.Com_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.MTV.Com-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron felt that whether or not the Jake and Neytiri love story would be perceived as believable partially hinged on the physical attractiveness of Neytiri's alien appearance, which was developed by considering her appeal to the all-male crew of artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-io9.com_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-io9.com-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Though Cameron felt Jake and Neytiri do not fall in love right away, their portrayers (<a href="#Worthington">Worthington</a> and <a href="#Saldana">Saldana</a>) felt the characters do. Cameron said the two actors "had a great chemistry" during filming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.MTV.Com_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-www.MTV.Com-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HuangShan.JPG"><img alt="A gray mountain in the middle of a forest." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3888" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/HuangShan.JPG/220px-HuangShan.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/HuangShan.JPG/330px-HuangShan.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/HuangShan.JPG/440px-HuangShan.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HuangShan.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pandora's floating "Hallelujah Mountains" were inspired in part by the Chinese <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Huang" title="Mount Huang">Huang Shan</a> mountains (pictured).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>For the film's floating "Hallelujah Mountains", the designers drew inspiration from "many different types of mountains, but mainly the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karst_topography" title="Karst topography">karst limestone</a> formations in China."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1o9speak_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-1o9speak-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> According to production designer Dylan Cole, the fictional floating rocks were inspired by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mount_Huang" title="Mount Huang">Mount Huang</a> (also known as Huangshan), <a href="/wiki/Guilin" title="Guilin">Guilin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zhangjiajie" title="Zhangjiajie">Zhangjiajie</a>, among others around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1o9speak_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-1o9speak-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> Director Cameron had noted the influence of the Chinese peaks on the design of the floating mountains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Renjie2010_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-Renjie2010-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>To create the interiors of the human mining colony on Pandora, production designers visited the <i><a href="/wiki/Noble_Corporation" title="Noble Corporation">Noble</a> Clyde Boudreaux</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NobleClydeBoudreaux_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-NobleClydeBoudreaux-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> oil platform in the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> during <span class="nowrap">June 2007</span>. They photographed, measured and filmed every aspect of the platform, which was later replicated on-screen with photorealistic <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">CGI</a> during post-production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DrillingRig_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-DrillingRig-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cameron said that he wanted to make "something that has this spoonful of sugar of all the action and the adventure and all that" but also have a conscience "that maybe in the enjoying of it makes you think a little bit about the way you interact with nature and your fellow man". He added that "the Na'vi represent something that is our higher selves, or our aspirational selves, what we would like to think we are" and that even though there are good humans within the film, the humans "represent what we know to be the parts of ourselves that are trashing our world and maybe condemning ourselves to a grim future".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Avatar_Friday_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Avatar_Friday-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cameron acknowledges that <i>Avatar</i> implicitly criticizes the United States' role in the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a> and the impersonal nature of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mechanized_warfare" title="Mechanized warfare">mechanized warfare</a> in general. In reference to the use of the term <i><a href="/wiki/Shock_and_awe" title="Shock and awe">shock and awe</a></i> in the film, Cameron said, "We know what it feels like to launch the missiles. We don't know what it feels like for them to land on our home soil, not in America."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoyle2009_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyle2009-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> He said in later interviews, "... I think it's very patriotic to question a system that needs to be corralled ..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup> and, "The film is definitely not anti-American."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimesqa_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimesqa-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> A scene in the film portrays the violent destruction of the towering Na'vi Hometree, which collapses in flames after a missile attack, coating the landscape with ash and floating embers. Asked about the scene's resemblance to the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a> on the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center" title="World Trade Center">World Trade Center</a>, Cameron said he had been "surprised at how much it did look like <span class="nowrap">September 11</span>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hoyle2009_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hoyle2009-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Filming">Filming</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">Principal photography</a> for <i>Avatar</i> began in <span class="nowrap">April 2007</span> in Los Angeles and <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>, New Zealand. Cameron described the film as a hybrid with a full live-action shoot in combination with computer-generated characters and live environments. "Ideally at the end of the day the audience has no idea which they're looking at," Cameron said. The director indicated that he had already worked four months on nonprincipal scenes for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> The live action was shot with a modified version of the proprietary digital 3-D <a href="/wiki/Fusion_Camera_System" title="Fusion Camera System">Fusion Camera System</a>, developed by Cameron and Vince Pace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-popularmechanics_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-popularmechanics-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> In <span class="nowrap">January 2007</span>, Fox had announced that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3-D_film" title="3-D film">3-D</a> filming for <i>Avatar</i> would be done at 24 frames per second despite Cameron's strong opinion that a 3-D film requires higher <a href="/wiki/Frame_rate" title="Frame rate">frame rate</a> to make <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Strobing" title="Strobing">strobing</a> less noticeable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Cameron, the film is composed of 60% computer-generated elements and 40% live action, as well as traditional <a href="/wiki/Miniature_effect" title="Miniature effect">miniatures</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epic1_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-epic1-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Motion-capture photography lasted 31 days at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hughes_Aircraft" title="Hughes Aircraft">Hughes Aircraft</a> stage in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Playa_Vista,_Los_Angeles,_California" title="Playa Vista, Los Angeles, California">Playa Vista</a> in Los Angeles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quittner_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-quittner-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Live action photography began in <span class="nowrap">October 2007</span> at Stone Street Studios in <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>, New Zealand, and was scheduled to last 31 days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> More than a thousand people worked on the production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-quittner_89-1"><a href="#cite_note-quittner-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> In preparation of the filming sequences, all of the actors underwent professional training specific to their characters such as archery, horseback riding, firearm use, and hand-to-hand combat. They received language and dialect training in the Na'vi language created for the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-makingofavatar_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-makingofavatar-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> Before shooting the film, Cameron also sent the cast to the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_tropical_rainforests" title="Hawaiian tropical rainforests">Hawaiian tropical rainforests</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> to get a feel for a rainforest setting before shooting on the soundstage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-makingofavatar_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-makingofavatar-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During filming, Cameron made use of his <a href="/wiki/Virtual_camera_system" title="Virtual camera system">virtual camera system</a>, a new way of directing motion-capture filmmaking. The system shows the actors' virtual counterparts in their digital surroundings in real time, allowing the director to adjust and direct scenes just as if shooting live action. According to Cameron, "It's like a big, powerful <a href="/wiki/Game_engine" title="Game engine">game engine</a>. If I want to fly through space, or change my perspective, I can. I can turn the whole scene into a living miniature and go through it on a 50 to 1 scale."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Waxmantimes_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Waxmantimes-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> Using conventional techniques, the complete virtual world cannot be seen until the motion-capture of the actors is complete. Cameron said this process does not diminish the value or importance of acting. On the contrary, because there is no need for repeated camera and lighting setups, costume fittings and make-up touch-ups, scenes do not need to be interrupted repeatedly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chicagotribune.com_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-chicagotribune.com-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron described the system as a "form of pure creation where if you want to move a tree or a mountain or the sky or change the time of day, you have complete control over the elements".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cameron gave fellow directors <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">Peter Jackson</a> a chance to test the new technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-king_68-1"><a href="#cite_note-king-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> Spielberg said, "I like to think of it as digital makeup, not augmented animation ... Motion capture brings the director back to a kind of intimacy that actors and directors only know when they're working in live theater."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chicagotribune.com_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-chicagotribune.com-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup> Spielberg and <a href="/wiki/George_Lucas" title="George Lucas">George Lucas</a> were also able to visit the set to watch Cameron direct with the equipment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-media-freaks.com_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-media-freaks.com-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>To film the shots where CGI interacts with live action, a unique camera referred to as a "simulcam" was used, a merger of the 3-D fusion camera and the virtual camera systems. While filming live action in real time with the simulcam, the CGI images captured with the virtual camera or designed from scratch, are superimposed over the live action images as in <a href="/wiki/Augmented_reality" title="Augmented reality">augmented reality</a> and shown on a small monitor, making it possible for the director to instruct the actors how to relate to the virtual material in the scene.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-makingofavatar_91-2"><a href="#cite_note-makingofavatar-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_effects">Visual effects</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Avatarmotioncapture.jpg"><img alt="The left image shows the blue cat-like alien Neyitiri shouting. The right image shows the actress who portrays her, Zoe Saldana, with motion-capture dots across her face and a small camera in front of her eyes." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="297" data-file-width="536" height="122" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5d/Avatarmotioncapture.jpg/220px-Avatarmotioncapture.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5d/Avatarmotioncapture.jpg/330px-Avatarmotioncapture.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/5d/Avatarmotioncapture.jpg/440px-Avatarmotioncapture.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Avatarmotioncapture.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cameron pioneered a specially designed camera built into a 6-inch boom that allowed the facial expressions of the actors to be captured and digitally recorded for the animators to use later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A number of innovative <a href="/wiki/Visual_effects" title="Visual effects">visual effects</a> techniques were used during production. According to Cameron, work on the film had been delayed since the 1990s to allow the techniques to reach the necessary degree of advancement to adequately portray his vision of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1996_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1996-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> The director planned to make use of photorealistic computer-generated characters, created using new <a href="/wiki/Motion_capture" title="Motion capture">motion capture</a> animation technologies he had been developing in the 14 months leading up to <span class="nowrap">December 2006</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Waxmantimes_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-Waxmantimes-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Innovations include a new system for lighting massive areas like Pandora's jungle,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.cnet.com_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-news.cnet.com-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motion_capture_stage" title="Motion capture stage">motion-capture stage</a> or "volume" six times larger than any previously used, and an improved method of capturing facial expressions, enabling full <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Performance_capture" title="Performance capture">performance capture</a>. To achieve the face capturing, actors wore individually made <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/skullcap#Noun" title="wikt:skullcap">skull caps</a> fitted with a tiny camera positioned in front of the actors' faces; the information collected about their facial expressions and eyes is then transmitted to computers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> According to Cameron, the method allows the filmmakers to transfer 100% of the actors' physical performances to their digital counterparts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup> Besides the performance capture data which were transferred directly to the computers, numerous reference cameras gave the digital artists multiple angles of each performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> A technically challenging scene was near the end of the film when the computer-generated Neytiri held the live action Jake in human form, and attention was given to the details of the shadows and reflected light between them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The lead visual effects company was <a href="/wiki/Weta_Digital" title="Weta Digital">Weta Digital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>, New Zealand, at one point employing 900 people to work on the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Because of the huge amount of data which needed to be stored, cataloged and available for everybody involved, even on the other side of the world, a new <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_Asset_Management" title="Digital Asset Management">Digital Asset Management</a> (DAM) system named Gaia was created by Microsoft especially for <i>Avatar</i>, which allowed the crews to keep track of and coordinate all stages in the digital processing.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> To render <i>Avatar</i>, Weta used a 10,000 sq ft (930 m<sup>2</sup>) <a href="/wiki/Server_farm" title="Server farm">server farm</a> making use of 4,000 <a href="/wiki/Hewlett-Packard" title="Hewlett-Packard">Hewlett-Packard</a> servers with 35,000 processor cores with 104 terabytes of RAM and three petabytes of network area storage running <a href="/wiki/Ubuntu_(operating_system)" title="Ubuntu (operating system)">Ubuntu</a> <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sun_Grid_Engine" title="Sun Grid Engine">Grid Engine</a> cluster manager, and 2 of the animation software and managers, Pixar's <a href="/wiki/RenderMan_(software)" title="RenderMan (software)">RenderMan</a> and Pixar's Alfred <a href="/wiki/Queue_management_system" title="Queue management system">queue management system</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Render_farm" title="Render farm">render farm</a> occupies the 193rd to 197th spots in the <a href="/wiki/TOP500" title="TOP500">TOP500</a> list of the world's most powerful <a href="/wiki/Supercomputer" title="Supercomputer">supercomputers</a>. A new texturing and paint software system, called Mari, was developed by The Foundry in cooperation with Weta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> Creating the Na'vi characters and the virtual world of Pandora required over a <a href="/wiki/Petabyte" title="Petabyte">petabyte</a> of digital storage,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> and each minute of the final footage for <i>Avatar</i> occupies 17.28 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gigabytes" title="Gigabytes">gigabytes</a> of storage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-datacenterknowledge_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-datacenterknowledge-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Often, it would take each frame of the movie several hours to render.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> To help finish preparing the special effects sequences on time, a number of other companies were brought on board, including <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Light_%26_Magic" title="Industrial Light &amp; Magic">Industrial Light &amp; Magic</a>, which worked alongside Weta Digital to create the battle sequences. ILM was responsible for the visual effects for many of the film's specialized vehicles and devised a new way to make CGI explosions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joe_Letteri" title="Joe Letteri">Joe Letteri</a> was the film's visual effects general supervisor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_soundtrack">Music and soundtrack</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Avatar:_Music_from_the_Motion_Picture" title="Avatar: Music from the Motion Picture">Avatar: Music from the Motion Picture</a></div>
<table class="mbox-small" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">

<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Composer <a href="/wiki/James_Horner" title="James Horner">James Horner</a> scored the film, his third collaboration with Cameron after <i><a href="/wiki/Aliens_(film)" title="Aliens (film)">Aliens</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Horner recorded parts of the score with a small chorus singing in the alien language Na'vi in <span class="nowrap">March 2008</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> He also worked with Wanda Bryant, an <a href="/wiki/Ethnomusicology" title="Ethnomusicology">ethnomusicologist</a>, to create a music culture for the alien race.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup> The first scoring sessions were planned to take place in early 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> During production, Horner promised Cameron that he would not work on any other project except for <i>Avatar</i> and reportedly worked on the score from four in the morning till ten at night throughout the process. He stated in an interview, "<i>Avatar</i> has been the most difficult film I have worked on and the biggest job I have undertaken."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Horner composed the score as two different scores merged into one. He first created a score that reflected the Na'vi way of sound and then combined it with a separate "traditional" score to drive the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-makingofavatar_91-3"><a href="#cite_note-makingofavatar-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> British singer <a href="/wiki/Leona_Lewis" title="Leona Lewis">Leona Lewis</a> was chosen to sing the theme song for the film, called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I_See_You_(Leona_Lewis_song)" title="I See You (Leona Lewis song)">I See You</a>". An accompanying music video, directed by <a href="/wiki/Jake_Nava" title="Jake Nava">Jake Nava</a>, premiered <span class="nowrap">December 15</span>, 2009, on MySpace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Promotions">Promotions</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JamesCameronCCJuly09.jpg"><img alt="James Cameron at the 2009 San Diego Comic-Con promoting Avatar." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="465" data-file-width="327" height="242" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/JamesCameronCCJuly09.jpg/170px-JamesCameronCCJuly09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/JamesCameronCCJuly09.jpg/255px-JamesCameronCCJuly09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/86/JamesCameronCCJuly09.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JamesCameronCCJuly09.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cameron at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con</a> promoting the film</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first photo of the film was released on <span class="nowrap">August 14</span>, 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empire_(magazine)" title="Empire (magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine released exclusive images from the film in its October issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron, producer <a href="/wiki/Jon_Landau_(film_producer)" title="Jon Landau (film producer)">Jon Landau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zoe_Saldana" title="Zoe Saldana">Zoe Saldana</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stephen_Lang_(actor)" title="Stephen Lang (actor)">Stephen Lang</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sigourney_Weaver" title="Sigourney Weaver">Sigourney Weaver</a> appeared at a panel, moderated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tom_Rothman" title="Tom Rothman">Tom Rothman</a>, at the 2009 <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_Comic-Con_International" title="San Diego Comic-Con International">San Diego Comic-Con</a> on <span class="nowrap">July 23</span>. Twenty-five minutes of footage was screened<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Dolby_3D" title="Dolby 3D">Dolby 3D</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> Weaver and Cameron appeared at additional panels to promote the film, speaking on the 23rd<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Comic-Con_Main_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Comic-Con_Main-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> and 24th<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Comic-Con_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-Comic-Con-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> respectively. James Cameron announced at the Comic-Con Avatar Panel that <span class="nowrap">August 21</span> will be 'Avatar Day'. On this day, the trailer was released in all theatrical formats. The official game trailer and toy line of the film were also unveiled on this day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The 129-second trailer was released online on <span class="nowrap">August 20</span>, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday1_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday1-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> The new 210-second trailer was premiered in theatres on <span class="nowrap">October 23</span>, 2009, then soon after premiered online on Yahoo! on <span class="nowrap">October 29</span>, 2009, to positive reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> An extended version in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IMAX_3D" title="IMAX 3D">IMAX 3D</a> received overwhelmingly positive reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usatoday1_129-1"><a href="#cite_note-usatoday1-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Hollywood Reporter</i> said that audience expectations were coloured by "the [same] establishment skepticism that preceded <i>Titanic</i>" and suggested the showing reflected the desire for original storytelling.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> The teaser has been among the most viewed trailers in the history of film marketing, reaching the first place of all trailers viewed on Apple.com with 4 million views.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> On October 30, to celebrate the opening of the first 3-D cinema in Vietnam, Fox allowed Megastar Cinema to screen exclusive 16 minutes of Avatar to a number of press.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> The three-and-a-half-minute trailer of the film premiered live on <span class="nowrap">November 1</span>, 2009, during a <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Cowboys" title="Dallas Cowboys">Dallas Cowboys</a> football game at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cowboys_Stadium" title="Cowboys Stadium">Cowboys Stadium</a> in Arlington, Texas, on the Diamond Vision screen, one of the world's largest video displays, and to TV audiences viewing the game on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NFL_on_Fox" title="NFL on Fox">Fox</a>. It is said to be the largest live motion picture trailer viewing in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="The Coca-Cola Company">The Coca-Cola Company</a> collaborated with Fox to launch a worldwide marketing campaign to promote the film. The highlight of the campaign was the website AVTR.com. Specially marked bottles and cans of <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Zero" title="Coca-Cola Zero">Coca-Cola Zero</a>, when held in front of a webcam, enabled users to interact with the website's 3-D features using augmented reality (AR) technology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> The film was heavily promoted in an episode of the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox Network</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Bones_(TV_series)" title="Bones (TV series)">Bones</a></i> in the episode "The Gamer In The Grease" (Season 5, Episode 9). <i>Avatar</i> star <a href="/wiki/Joel_David_Moore" title="Joel David Moore">Joel David Moore</a> has a recurring role on the program, and is seen in the episode anxiously awaiting the release of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> A week prior to the American release, Zoe Saldana promoted the film on <a href="/wiki/Adult_Swim" title="Adult Swim">Adult Swim</a> when she was interviewed by an animated <a href="/wiki/Space_Ghost" title="Space Ghost">Space Ghost</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> had a promotion mentioned in television commercials in Europe called "Avatarize yourself", which encouraged people to go to the website set up by <a href="/wiki/Oddcast_(company)" title="Oddcast (company)">Oddcast</a>, and use a photograph of themselves to change into a Na'vi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Books">Books</span></h3>
<p><i>Avatar: A Confidential Report on the Biological and Social History of Pandora</i>, a 224-page book in the form of a field guide to the film's fictional setting of the planet of Pandora, was released by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harper_Entertainment" title="Harper Entertainment">Harper Entertainment</a> on <span class="nowrap">November 24</span>, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Confidentialreport_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-Confidentialreport-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> It is presented as a compilation of data collected by the humans about Pandora and the life on it, written by Maria Wilhelm and Dirk Mathison. HarperFestival also released Wilhelm's 48-page <i>James Cameron's Avatar: The Reusable Scrapbook</i> for children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Art_of_Avatar" title="The Art of Avatar">The Art of Avatar</a></i> was released on <span class="nowrap">November 30</span>, 2009, by <a href="/wiki/Abrams_Books" title="Abrams Books">Abrams Books</a>. The book features detailed production artwork from the film, including production sketches, illustrations by Lisa Fitzpatrick, and film stills. Producer <a href="/wiki/Jon_Landau_(film_producer)" title="Jon Landau (film producer)">Jon Landau</a> wrote the foreword, Cameron wrote the epilogue, and director <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">Peter Jackson</a> wrote the preface.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> In <span class="nowrap">October 2010</span>, Abrams Books also released <i>The Making of Avatar</i>, a 272-page book that detailed the film's production process and contains over 500 color photographs and illustrations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In a 2009 interview, Cameron said that he planned to write a novel version of <i>Avatar</i> after the film was released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup> In <span class="nowrap">February 2010</span>, producer Jon Landau stated that Cameron plans a prequel novel for <i>Avatar</i> that will "lead up to telling the story of the movie, but it would go into much more depth about all the stories that we didn't have time to deal with", saying that "Jim wants to write a novel that is a big, epic story that fills in a lot of things".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 2013 it was announced that Cameron hired <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gould" title="Steven Gould">Steven Gould</a> to pen four standalone novels to expand the <i>Avatar</i> universe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Video_games">Video games</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron%27s_Avatar:_The_Game" title="James Cameron's Avatar: The Game">James Cameron's Avatar: The Game</a></div>
<p>Cameron chose <a href="/wiki/Ubisoft_Montreal" title="Ubisoft Montreal">Ubisoft Montreal</a> to create an <i>Avatar</i> game for the film in 2007. The filmmakers and game developers collaborated heavily, and Cameron decided to include some of Ubisoft's vehicle and creature designs into the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-e3_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-e3-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>James Cameron's Avatar: The Game</i> was released on <span class="nowrap">December 1</span>, 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> for most home video game consoles (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PS3" title="PS3">PS3</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wii" title="Wii">Wii</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nintendo_DS" title="Nintendo DS">Nintendo DS</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPhone_OS" title="IPhone OS">iPhone</a>), <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and <span class="nowrap">December 8</span> for <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PSP</a>.</p>
