<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Action_figures_and_postage_stamps">Action figures and postage stamps</span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mattel_Toys" title="Mattel Toys">Mattel Toys</a> announced in December 2009 that it would be introducing a line of <i>Avatar</i> action figures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-licensing.biz_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-licensing.biz-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> Each action figure will be made with a 3-D web tag, called an i-TAG, that consumers can scan using a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Web_camera" title="Web camera">web cam</a>, revealing unique on-screen content that is special to each specific action figure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-licensing.biz_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-licensing.biz-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> A series of toys representing six different characters from the film were also distributed in <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald's">McDonald's</a> <a href="/wiki/Happy_Meal" title="Happy Meal">Happy Meals</a> in Argentina, Brazil, Canada, China, <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a>, the United States and <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Avatar_toys_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-Avatar_toys-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2009, <a href="/wiki/La_Poste_(France)" title="La Poste (France)">France Post</a> released a special limited edition stamp based on <i>Avatar</i>, coinciding with the film's worldwide release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theme_park_attraction">Theme park attraction</span></h3>
<p>At <a href="/wiki/Disney_D23#2013" title="Disney D23">Disney's 2013 D23</a> event, <a href="/wiki/Avatar_Land" title="Avatar Land">a themed land based on <i>Avatar</i></a> was announced for <a href="/wiki/Disney%27s_Animal_Kingdom" title="Disney's Animal Kingdom">Disney's Animal Kingdom</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lake_Buena_Vista,_Florida" title="Lake Buena Vista, Florida">Lake Buena Vista, Florida</a>. Construction began in 2014 and is set to open in 2017.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Disney_to_build_Avatar_attractions_at_its_theme_parks_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Disney_to_build_Avatar_attractions_at_its_theme_parks-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_screening">Initial screening</span></h3>
<p><i>Avatar</i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Film_premiere" title="Film premiere">premiered</a> in London on <span class="nowrap">December 10</span>, 2009, and was released theatrically worldwide from <span class="nowrap">December 16</span> to 18.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-release-dates_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-release-dates-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> The film was originally set for release on <span class="nowrap">May 22</span>, 2009, during filming,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> but was pushed back to allow more post-production time (the last shots were delivered in November),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-news.cnet.com_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-news.cnet.com-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> and to give more time for theatres worldwide to install 3D projectors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron stated that the film's <a href="/wiki/Aspect_ratio_(image)" title="Aspect ratio (image)">aspect ratio</a> would be 1.78:1 for 3D screenings and that a 2.39:1 image would be extracted for 2D screenings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> However, a 3D 2.39:1 extract was approved for use with constant-image-height screens (i.e. screens which increase in width to display 2.39:1 films).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> During a 3D preview showing in Germany on <span class="nowrap">December 16</span>, the movie's <a href="/wiki/Digital_rights_management" title="Digital rights management">DRM</a> 'protection' system failed, and some copies delivered could not be watched at all in the theaters. The problems were fixed in time for the public premiere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drm_difficulties_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-drm_difficulties-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Avatar</i> was released in a total of 3,457 theatres in the US, of which 2,032 theatres ran it in 3D. In total 90% of all advance ticket sales for <i>Avatar</i> were for 3D screenings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Internationally, <i>Avatar</i> opened on a total of 14,604 screens in 106 territories, of which 3,671 were showing the film in 3D (producing 56% of the first weekend gross).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-.27Avatar.27_dominates_int.27l_boxoffice_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-.27Avatar.27_dominates_int.27l_boxoffice-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup> The film was simultaneously presented in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IMAX_3D" title="IMAX 3D">IMAX 3D</a> format, opening in 178 theaters in the United States on <span class="nowrap">December 18</span>. The international IMAX release included 58 theaters beginning on <span class="nowrap">December 16</span>, and 25 more theaters were to be added in the coming weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMAXrecord2_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-IMAXrecord2-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> The IMAX release was the company's widest to date, a total of 261 theaters worldwide. The previous IMAX record opening was <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Half-Blood_Prince_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince (film)">Harry Potter and the Half-Blood Prince</a></i>, which opened in 161 IMAX theatres in the US, and about 70 international.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> 20th Century Fox Korea adapted and later released <i>Avatar</i> in <a href="/wiki/4D_film" title="4D film">4D version</a>, which included "moving seats, smells of explosives, sprinkling water, laser lights and wind".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4-D_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-4-D-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="General">General</span></h4>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_box_office_records_set_by_Avatar" title="List of box office records set by Avatar">List of box office records set by Avatar</a></div>
<p><i>Avatar</i> was released internationally on more than 14,000 screens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Avatar</i> earned $3,537,000 from midnight screenings <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Domestic_box_office" title="Domestic box office">domestically</a> (United States and Canada), with the initial 3D release limited to 2,200 screens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> The film earned $26,752,099 on its opening day, and $77,025,481 over its opening weekend, making it the second largest December opening ever behind <i><a href="/wiki/I_Am_Legend_(film)" title="I Am Legend (film)">I Am Legend</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxofficemojo_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Boxofficemojo-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.comingsoon.net_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-www.comingsoon.net-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> the largest domestic opening weekend for a film not based on a franchise (topping <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Incredibles_(film)" title="The Incredibles (film)">The Incredibles</a></i>), the highest opening weekend for a film entirely in 3D (breaking <i><a href="/wiki/Up_(2009_film)" title="Up (2009 film)">Up</a></i> '​s record),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup> the highest opening weekend for an environmentalist film (breaking <i><a href="/wiki/The_Day_After_Tomorrow" title="The Day After Tomorrow">The Day After Tomorrow</a></i> '​s record),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> and the 40th largest opening weekend in North America,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxofficemojo_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-Boxofficemojo-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> despite <a href="/wiki/North_American_blizzard_of_2009" title="North American blizzard of 2009">a blizzard</a> which blanketed the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast of the United States</a> and reportedly hurt its opening weekend results.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.nytimes.com_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-www.nytimes.com-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.comingsoon.net_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-www.comingsoon.net-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.reuters.com_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-www.reuters.com-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> The film also set an IMAX opening weekend record, with 178 theaters generating approximately $9.5 million, 12% of the film's $77 million (at the time) North American gross on less than 3% of the screens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMAXrecord2_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-IMAXrecord2-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>International markets generating opening weekend tallies of at least $10 million were Russia ($19.7 million), France ($17.4 million), the UK ($13.8 million), Germany ($13.3 million), South Korea ($11.7 million), Australia ($11.5 million) and Spain ($11.0 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Avatar'</i>s worldwide gross was US$241.6 million after five days, the ninth largest opening-weekend gross of all time, and the largest for a non-franchise, non-sequel and original film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup> 58 international IMAX screens generated an estimated $4.1 million during the opening weekend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IMAXrecord2_163-2"><a href="#cite_note-IMAXrecord2-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Revenues in the film's second weekend decreased by only 1.8% in domestic markets, marking a rare occurrence,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.marketwatch.com_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.marketwatch.com-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> earning $75,617,183, to remain in first place at the box office<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> and recording the biggest second weekend of all time<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup> (since surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Marvel_Entertainment" title="Marvel Entertainment">Marvel's</a> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Avengers_(2012_film)" title="The Avengers (2012 film)">The Avengers</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> The film experienced another marginal decrease in revenue in its third weekend, dropping 9.4% to $68,490,688 domestically, remaining in first place at the box office,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup> to set a third-weekend record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Avatar</i> crossed the $1 <a href="/wiki/1,000,000,000" title="1,000,000,000">billion</a> mark on the 19th day of its international release, making it the first film to reach this mark in only 19 days<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxoffice3_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxoffice3-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup> (a record now matched by both <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_%E2%80%93_Part_2" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows – Part 2</a></i> in 2011 and <i>The Avengers</i> in 2012).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1billionmarkmatched_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-1billionmarkmatched-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> It became the fifth film grossing more than $1 billion worldwide, and the only film of <a href="/wiki/2009_in_film" title="2009 in film">2009</a> to do so.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2009_worldwide_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-2009_worldwide-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup> In its fourth weekend, <i>Avatar</i> continued to lead the box office domestically, setting a new all-time fourth-weekend record of $50,306,217,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> and becoming the highest-grossing 2009 release in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WWW.marketwatch.com_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-WWW.marketwatch.com-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> In the film's fifth weekend, it set the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King_Day" title="Martin Luther King Day">Martin Luther King Day</a> four-day weekend record, grossing $54,401,446,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup> and set a fifth-weekend record with a take of $42,785,612.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> It held to the top spot to set the sixth and seventh weekend records earning $34,944,081<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup> and $31,280,029<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup> respectively. It was (and still is) the fastest film to gross $600 million domestically, on its 47th day in theatres.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On <span class="nowrap">January 31</span>, it became the first film to earn over <span class="nowrap">$2 billion</span> worldwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Deprez2010_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-Deprez2010-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup> and it became the first film to gross over <span class="nowrap">$700 million</span> in North America, on <span class="nowrap">February 27</span>, after 72 days of release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup> It remained in the number one spot at the domestic box office for seven consecutive weeks – the most consecutive No. 1 weekends since <i>Titanic</i> spent 15 weekends at No. 1 in 1997–'98<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> – and also spent 11 consecutive weekends at the top of the box office outside the United States and Canada, breaking the record of 9 consecutive weekends set by <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_Dead_Man%27s_Chest" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man's Chest">Pirates of the Caribbean: Dead Man's Chest</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup> By the end of its first theatrical release <i>Avatar</i> had grossed $749,766,139 in the U.S. and Canada, and $1,999,298,189 in other territories, for a worldwide total of $2,749,064,328.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxofficemojo_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-Boxofficemojo-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Including the revenue from a <a href="#Extended_theatrical_re-release">re-release of <i>Avatar</i></a> featuring extended footage, <i>Avatar</i> grossed $760,507,625 in the U.S. and Canada, and $2,027,457,462 in other territories for a worldwide total of $2,787,965,087<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxofficemojo_7-4"><a href="#cite_note-Boxofficemojo-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxoffice2_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-boxoffice2-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> with 72.7% of its total worldwide gross in international markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxofficemojo_7-5"><a href="#cite_note-Boxofficemojo-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxoffice2_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-boxoffice2-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Avatar</i> has set a number of box office records during its release: on <span class="nowrap">January 25</span>, 2010, it surpassed <i>Titanic'</i>s worldwide gross to become the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">highest-grossing film of all time worldwide</a> 41 days after its international release,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.hollywoodreporter.com_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.hollywoodreporter.com-192"><span>[</span>192<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193"><span>[</span>193<span>]</span></a></sup> just two days after taking the foreign box office record,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray_.28February_3.2C_2010.29_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gray_.28February_3.2C_2010.29-194"><span>[</span>194<span>]</span></a></sup> and on <span class="nowrap">February 2</span>, 47 days after its domestic release, <i>Avatar</i> surpassed <i>Titanic</i> to become the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films_in_Canada_and_the_United_States" title="List of highest-grossing films in Canada and the United States">highest-grossing film of all time</a> in Canada and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195"><span>[</span>195<span>]</span></a></sup> It became the highest-grossing film of all time in at least 30 other countries<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxoffice4_196-0"><a href="#cite_note-boxoffice4-196"><span>[</span>196<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197"><span>[</span>197<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198"><span>[</span>198<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199"><span>[</span>199<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200"><span>[</span>200<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201"><span>[</span>201<span>]</span></a></sup> and is the first film to earn over $2 billion in foreign box office receipts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boxofficemojoalltime_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-boxofficemojoalltime-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> IMAX ticket sales account for $228 million of its worldwide gross,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202"><span>[</span>202<span>]</span></a></sup> more than double the previous record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imaxrecord_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-imaxrecord-203"><span>[</span>203<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Box_Office_Mojo" title="Box Office Mojo">Box Office Mojo</a> estimates that after adjusting for the rise in average ticket prices, <i>Avatar</i> would be the 14th-highest-grossing film of all time in North America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204"><span>[</span>204<span>]</span></a></sup> Box Office Mojo also observes that the higher ticket prices for 3D and IMAX screenings have had a significant impact on <i>Avatar's</i> gross; it estimated, on <span class="nowrap">April 21</span>, 2010, that <i>Avatar</i> had sold approximately <span class="nowrap">75 million</span> tickets in North American theatres, more than any other film since 1999's <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Episode_I:_The_Phantom_Menace" title="Star Wars Episode I: The Phantom Menace">Star Wars Episode I: The Phantom Menace</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ray_Subers_.282010-04-21.29_205-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ray_Subers_.282010-04-21.29-205"><span>[</span>205<span>]</span></a></sup> On a worldwide basis, <i>Avatar</i> ranks third after adjusting for inflation, behind <i><a href="/wiki/Gone_with_the_Wind_(film)" title="Gone with the Wind (film)">Gone with the Wind</a></i> and <i>Titanic</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206"><span>[</span>206<span>]</span></a></sup> although some reports place it ahead of <i>Titanic</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207"><span>[</span>207<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_analysis">Commercial analysis</span></h4>
<p>Before its release, various film critics and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fanboy" title="Fanboy">fan communities</a> predicted the film would be a <a href="/wiki/Box_office_bomb" title="Box office bomb">significant disappointment at the box office</a>, in line with predictions made for Cameron's previous blockbuster <i>Titanic</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.slate.com_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.slate.com-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn.com_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210"><span>[</span>210<span>]</span></a></sup> This criticism ranged from <i>Avatar'</i>s film budget, to its concept and use of 3-D "blue cat people".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.slate.com_208-1"><a href="#cite_note-www.slate.com-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn.com_209-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Slate_(magazine)" title="Slate (magazine)">Slate</a></i> magazine's Daniel Engber complimented the 3D effects, but criticized them for reminding him of certain CGI characters from the <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a></i> prequel films and for having the "<a href="/wiki/Uncanny_valley" title="Uncanny valley">uncanny valley</a>" effect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Slate_Engber_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-Slate_Engber-211"><span>[</span>211<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The New York Times</i> noted that 20th Century Fox executives had decided to release <i><a href="/wiki/Alvin_and_the_Chipmunks:_The_Squeakquel" title="Alvin and the Chipmunks: The Squeakquel">Alvin and the Chipmunks: The Squeakquel</a></i> alongside <i>Avatar</i>, calling it a "secret weapon" to cover any unforeseeable losses at the box-office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212"><span>[</span>212<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:30%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I think if everybody was embracing the film before the fact, the film could never live up to that expectation ... Have them go with some sense of wanting to find the answer."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">James Cameron on criticism of <i>Avatar</i> before its release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn.com_209-2"><a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>Box office analysts, on the other hand, estimated that the film would be a box office success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.slate.com_208-2"><a href="#cite_note-www.slate.com-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.MTV.com_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.MTV.com-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> "The holy grail of 3-D has finally arrived," said an analyst for Exhibitor Relations. "This is why all these 3-D venues were built: for <i>Avatar.</i> This is the one. The behemoth."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.MTV.com_213-1"><a href="#cite_note-www.MTV.com-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup> The "cautionary estimate" was that <i>Avatar</i> would bring in around $60 million in its opening weekend. Others guessed higher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.MTV.com_213-2"><a href="#cite_note-www.MTV.com-213"><span>[</span>213<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hollywood_Elsewhere_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hollywood_Elsewhere-214"><span>[</span>214<span>]</span></a></sup> There were also analysts who believed that the film's three-dimensionality would help its box office performance, given that recent 3D films had been successful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.slate.com_208-3"><a href="#cite_note-www.slate.com-208"><span>[</span>208<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cameron said he felt the pressure of the predictions, but that pressure is good for film-makers. "It makes us think about our audiences and what the audience wants," he stated. "We owe them a good time. We owe them a piece of good entertainment."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn.com_209-3"><a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> Although he felt <i>Avatar</i> would appeal to everyone and that the film could not afford to have a target <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demographics" title="Demographics">demographic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn.com_209-4"><a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> he especially wanted hard-core science-fiction fans to see it: "If I can just get 'em in the damn theater, the film will act on them in the way it's supposed to, in terms of taking them on an amazing journey and giving them this rich emotional experience."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SciFiWire_215-0"><a href="#cite_note-SciFiWire-215"><span>[</span>215<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron was aware of the sentiment that <i>Avatar</i> would need significant "repeat business" just to make up for its budget and achieve box office success, and believed <i>Avatar</i> could inspire the same "sharing" reaction as <i>Titanic</i>. He said that film worked because, "When people have an experience that's very powerful in the movie theatre, they want to go share it. They want to grab their friend and bring them, so that they can enjoy it. They want to be the person to bring them the news that this is something worth having in their life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn.com_209-5"><a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After the film's release and unusually strong box office performance over its first two weeks, it was debated as the one film capable of surpassing <i>Titanic'</i>s worldwide gross, and its continued strength perplexed box office analysts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-omg.yahoo.com_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-omg.yahoo.com-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> Other films in recent years had been cited as contenders for surpassing <i>Titanic</i>, such as 2008's <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manolith.com_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-manolith.com-217"><span>[</span>217<span>]</span></a></sup> but <i>Avatar</i> was considered the first film with a genuine chance to do so, and its numbers being aided by higher ticket prices for 3D screenings<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-omg.yahoo.com_216-1"><a href="#cite_note-omg.yahoo.com-216"><span>[</span>216<span>]</span></a></sup> did not fully explain its success to box office analysts. "Most films are considered to be healthy if they manage anything less than a 50% drop from their first weekend to their second. Dipping just 11% from the first to the third is unheard of," said Paul Dergarabedian, president of box-office analysis for Hollywood.com. "This is just unprecedented. I had to do a double take. I thought it was a miscalculation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.marketwatch.com_171-1"><a href="#cite_note-www.marketwatch.com-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> Analysts predicted second place for the film's worldwide gross, but most were uncertain about it surpassing <i>Titanic</i> because "Today's films flame out much faster than they did when <i>Titanic</i> was released."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.marketwatch.com_171-2"><a href="#cite_note-www.marketwatch.com-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> Brandon Gray, president of Box Office Mojo, believed in the film's chances of becoming the highest-grossing film of all time, though he also believed it was too early to surmise because it had only played during the holidays. He said, "While <i>Avatar</i> may beat <i>Titanic's</i> revenue record, it will be tough, and the film is unlikely to surpass <i>Titanic</i> in attendance. Ticket prices were about $3 cheaper in the late 1990s."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.marketwatch.com_171-3"><a href="#cite_note-www.marketwatch.com-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron said he did not think it was realistic to "try to topple <i>Titanic</i> off its perch" because it "just struck some kind of chord" and there had been other good films in recent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.mtv.com_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.mtv.com-218"><span>[</span>218<span>]</span></a></sup> He changed his prediction by mid-January. "It's gonna happen. It's just a matter of time," he said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219"><span>[</span>219<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:35%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"You've got to compete head on with these other epic works of fantasy and fiction, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tolkien#Writing" title="Tolkien">Tolkiens</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars" title="Star Wars">Star Wars</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Star_Trek" title="Star Trek">Star Treks</a>. People want a persistent alternate reality to invest themselves in and they want the detail that makes it rich and worth their time. They want to live somewhere else. Like <a href="/wiki/Fictional_universe_of_Avatar#Astronomy_and_geology" title="Fictional universe of Avatar">Pandora</a>."</p>
</div>
</div>
<div style="text-align: left;">James Cameron on the success of <i>Avatar</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220"><span>[</span>220<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
<p>Though analysts have been unable to agree that <i>Avatar'</i>s success is attributable to one primary factor, several explanations have been advanced. First, January is historically "the dumping ground for the year's weakest films", and this also applied to 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.newsweek.com_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-www.newsweek.com-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron himself said he decided to open the film in December so that it would have less competition from then to January.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnn.com_209-6"><a href="#cite_note-cnn.com-209"><span>[</span>209<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Titanic</i> capitalized on the same January predictability, and earned most of its gross in 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.newsweek.com_221-1"><a href="#cite_note-www.newsweek.com-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> Additionally, <i>Avatar</i> established itself as a "must-see" event. Gray said, "At this point, people who are going to see <i>Avatar</i> are going to see <i>Avatar</i> and would even if the slate was strong."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.newsweek.com_221-2"><a href="#cite_note-www.newsweek.com-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> Marketing the film as a "novelty factor" also helped. Fox positioned the film as a cinematic event that should be seen in the theatres. "It's really hard to sell the idea that you can have the same experience at home," stated David Mumpower, an analyst at BoxOfficeProphets.com.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.newsweek.com_221-3"><a href="#cite_note-www.newsweek.com-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> The "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Oscar</a> buzz" surrounding the film and international viewings helped. "Two-thirds of <i>Titanic's</i> haul was earned overseas, and <i>Avatar</i> [tracked] similarly ...<i>Avatar</i> opened in 106 markets globally and was No. 1 in all of them", and the markets "such as Russia, where <i>Titanic</i> saw modest receipts in 1997 and 1998, are white-hot today" with "more screens and moviegoers" than before.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.newsweek.com_221-4"><a href="#cite_note-www.newsweek.com-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i>, films in 3D accumulated $1.3 billion in 2009, "a threefold increase over 2008 and more than 10% of the total 2009 box-office gross". The increased ticket price – an average of $2 to $3 per ticket in most markets – helped the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.newsweek.com_221-5"><a href="#cite_note-www.newsweek.com-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup> Likewise, <i>Entertainment Weekly</i> attributed the film's success to 3D glasses, but also to its "astronomic <a href="/wiki/Word_of_mouth" title="Word of mouth">word-of-mouth</a>". Not only do some theaters charge up to $18.50 for IMAX tickets, but "the buzz" created by the new technology was the possible cause for sold-out screenings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hollywoodinsider.ew.com_222-0"><a href="#cite_note-hollywoodinsider.ew.com-222"><span>[</span>222<span>]</span></a></sup> Gray said <i>Avatar</i> having no basis in previously established material makes its performance remarkable and even more impressive. "The movie might be derivative of many movies in its story and themes," he said, "but it had no direct antecedent like the other top-grossing films: <i>Titanic</i> (historical events), the <i>Star Wars</i> movies (an established film franchise), or <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> (literature). It was a tougher sell ..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-www.newsweek.com_221-6"><a href="#cite_note-www.newsweek.com-221"><span>[</span>221<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception <span id="Critics"></span></span></h3>
<dl>
<dd><i>See also: <a href="/wiki/Themes_in_Avatar" title="Themes in Avatar">Themes in Avatar</a> for more reviews</i></dd>
</dl>
<p>The film received mostly positive reviews. Review aggregator <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> reports that 83% of 292 professional critics have given the film a positive review, with a rating average of 7.4 out of 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rottentomatoes_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-rottentomatoes-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> The site's consensus is that "It might be more impressive on a technical level than as a piece of storytelling, but <i>Avatar</i> reaffirms James Cameron's singular gift for imaginative, absorbing filmmaking."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rottentomatoes_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-rottentomatoes-223"><span>[</span>223<span>]</span></a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean">weighted mean</a> rating out of 100 reviews from film critics, the film has a "universal acclaim" rating score of 83 based on 35 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224"><span>[</span>224<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a> polls conducted during the opening weekend revealed the average grade cinemagoers gave <i>Avatar</i> was A on an A+ to F scale. Every demographic surveyed was reported to give this rating. These polls also indicated that the main draw of the film was its use of <a href="/wiki/3D_film" title="3D film">3D</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225"><span>[</span>225<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> called the film "extraordinary" and gave it four stars out of four. "Watching <i>Avatar</i>, I felt sort of the same as when I saw <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Star_Wars_Episode_IV:_A_New_Hope" title="Star Wars Episode IV: A New Hope">Star Wars</a></i> in 1977", he said, adding that like <i>Star Wars</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Fellowship of the Ring">The Lord of the Rings</a></i>, the film "employs a new generation of special effects" and it "is not simply a sensational entertainment, although it is that. It's a technical breakthrough. It has a flat-out Green and anti-war message".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rogerebert.suntimes_226-0"><a href="#cite_note-rogerebert.suntimes-226"><span>[</span>226<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott">A. O. Scott</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/At_the_Movies_(U.S._TV_series)" title="At the Movies (U.S. TV series)">At The Movies</a></i> also compared his viewing of the film to the first time he viewed <i>Star Wars</i>, and added that although "the script is a little bit ... obvious," it was "part of what made it work".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A._O._Scott_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-A._O._Scott-227"><span>[</span>227<span>]</span></a></sup> Todd McCarthy of <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> praised the film. "The King of the World sets his sights on creating another world entirely in <i>Avatar</i>, and it's very much a place worth visiting."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228"><span>[</span>228<span>]</span></a></sup> Kirk Honeycutt of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> gave the film a positive review. "The screen is alive with more action and the soundtrack pops with more robust music than any dozen sci-fi shoot-'em-ups you care to mention" he stated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229"><span>[</span>229<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Rolling Stone</i> film critic <a href="/wiki/Peter_Travers" title="Peter Travers">Peter Travers</a> awarded <i>Avatar</i> three and a half out of four stars and wrote in his print review, "It extends the possibilities of what movies can do. Cameron's talent may just be as big as his dreams."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-230"><a href="#cite_note-230"><span>[</span>230<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Corliss" title="Richard Corliss">Richard Corliss</a> of <i>Time</i> magazine thought that the film was, "the most vivid and convincing creation of a fantasy world ever seen in the history of moving pictures."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231"><span>[</span>231<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Turan" title="Kenneth Turan">Kenneth Turan</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> felt the film has "powerful" visual accomplishments but "flat dialogue" and "obvious characterization".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Turan2009_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-Turan2009-232"><span>[</span>232<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Berardinelli" title="James Berardinelli">James Berardinelli</a>, film critic for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ReelViews" title="ReelViews">ReelViews</a>, praised the film and its story, giving it four out of four stars; he wrote, "In 3-D, it's immersive – but the traditional film elements – story, character, editing, theme, emotional resonance, etc. – are presented with sufficient expertise to make even the 2-D version an engrossing 2½-hour experience."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233"><span>[</span>233<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Avatar'</i>s underlying social and political themes attracted attention. <a href="/wiki/Armond_White" title="Armond White">Armond White</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Press" title="New York Press">New York Press</a></i> wrote that Cameron used villainous American characters to misrepresent facets of <a href="/wiki/Militarism" title="Militarism">militarism</a>, capitalism, and <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">imperialism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234"><span>[</span>234<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235"><span>[</span>235<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Evo_Morales" title="Evo Morales">Evo Morales</a>, Bolivia's first indigenous president, praised the film for its "profound show of resistance to capitalism and the struggle for the defense of nature".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236"><span>[</span>236<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russell_D._Moore" title="Russell D. Moore">Russell D. Moore</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Christian_Post" title="The Christian Post">The Christian Post</a></i> concluded that propaganda exists in the film and stated, "If you can get a theater full of people in <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">Kentucky</a> to stand and applaud the defeat of their country in war, then you've got some amazing special effects."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237"><span>[</span>237<span>]</span></a></sup> Some commentators sympathetic to <a href="/wiki/Anarcho-primitivism" title="Anarcho-primitivism">anarcho-primitivism</a> have even praised the film as a manifesto for their cause.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-infoshop_238-0"><a href="#cite_note-infoshop-238"><span>[</span>238<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zerzan_239-0"><a href="#cite_note-zerzan-239"><span>[</span>239<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adam_Cohen_(journalist)" title="Adam Cohen (journalist)">Adam Cohen</a> of <i>The New York Times</i> was more positive about the film, calling its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-imperialist" title="Anti-imperialist">anti-imperialist</a> message "a 22nd-century version of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American colonists vs. the British</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">India vs. the Raj</a>, or Latin America vs. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Fruit" title="United Fruit">United Fruit</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTeditorial_240-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTeditorial-240"><span>[</span>240<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ross_Douthat" title="Ross Douthat">Ross Douthat</a> of <i>The New York Times</i> opined that the film is "Cameron's long <a href="/wiki/Apologia" title="Apologia">apologia</a> for <a href="/wiki/Pantheism" title="Pantheism">pantheism</a> ... Hollywood's religion of choice for a generation now",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241"><span>[</span>241<span>]</span></a></sup> while Saritha Prabhu of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tennessean" title="The Tennessean">The Tennessean</a></i> called the film a misportrayal of pantheism and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_religion" title="Eastern religion">Eastern spirituality</a> in general,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242"><span>[</span>242<span>]</span></a></sup> and Maxim Osipov of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Hindustan_Times" title="The Hindustan Times">The Hindustan Times</a></i>, on the contrary, commended the film's message for its overall consistency with the teachings of Hinduism in the <a href="/wiki/Bhagavad_Gita" title="Bhagavad Gita">Bhagavad Gita</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243"><span>[</span>243<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Annalee_Newitz" title="Annalee Newitz">Annalee Newitz</a> of <a href="/wiki/Io9" title="Io9">io9</a> concluded that <i>Avatar</i> is another film that has the recurring "fantasy about race" whereby "some white guy" becomes the "most awesome" member of a non-white culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Newitz2009_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-Newitz2009-244"><span>[</span>244<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Phillips_(critic)" title="Michael Phillips (critic)">Michael Phillips</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> called <i>Avatar</i> "the season's ideological <a href="/wiki/Rorschach_test" title="Rorschach test">Rorschach blot</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245"><span>[</span>245<span>]</span></a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Miranda_Devine" title="Miranda Devine">Miranda Devine</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sydney_Morning_Herald" title="The Sydney Morning Herald">The Sydney Morning Herald</a></i> felt that, "It is impossible to watch Avatar without being banged over the head with the director's ideological hammer."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Devine2010_246-0"><a href="#cite_note-Devine2010-246"><span>[</span>246<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Critics and audiences have cited similarities with other films, literature or media, describing the perceived connections in ways ranging from simple "borrowing" to outright plagiarism. <a href="/wiki/Ty_Burr" title="Ty Burr">Ty Burr</a> of the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boston_Globe" title="Boston Globe">Boston Globe</a></i> called it "the same movie" as <i><a href="/wiki/Dances_with_Wolves" title="Dances with Wolves">Dances with Wolves</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burr2009_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burr2009-247"><span>[</span>247<span>]</span></a></sup> Like <i>Dances with Wolves</i>, <i>Avatar</i> has been characterized as being a <a href="/wiki/White_savior_narrative_in_film" title="White savior narrative in film">"white savior" movie</a>, in which a "backwards" native people is impotent without the leadership of a member of the invading white culture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barnard2010_248-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barnard2010-248"><span>[</span>248<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249"><span>[</span>249<span>]</span></a></sup> Parallels to the concept and use of an avatar are in <a href="/wiki/Poul_Anderson" title="Poul Anderson">Poul Anderson's</a> 1957 novelette "<a href="/wiki/Call_Me_Joe" title="Call Me Joe">Call Me Joe</a>", in which a paralyzed man uses his mind from orbit to control an artificial body on Jupiter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250"><span>[</span>250<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Westfahl2009_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-Westfahl2009-251"><span>[</span>251<span>]</span></a></sup> Cinema audiences in Russia have noted that <i>Avatar</i> has elements in common with the 1960s <i><a href="/wiki/Noon_Universe" title="Noon Universe">Noon Universe</a></i> novels by <a href="/wiki/Arkady_and_Boris_Strugatsky" title="Arkady and Boris Strugatsky">Arkady and Boris Strugatsky</a>, which are set in the 22nd century on a forested world called Pandora with a sentient indigenous species called the Nave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harding_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harding-252"><span>[</span>252<span>]</span></a></sup> Various reviews have compared <i>Avatar</i> to the films <i><a href="/wiki/FernGully:_The_Last_Rainforest" title="FernGully: The Last Rainforest">FernGully: The Last Rainforest</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253"><span>[</span>253<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254"><span>[</span>254<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Pocahontas_(1995_film)" title="Pocahontas (1995 film)">Pocahontas</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255"><span>[</span>255<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Samurai" title="The Last Samurai">The Last Samurai</a>.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256"><span>[</span>256<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/NPR" title="NPR">NPR</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Morning_Edition" title="Morning Edition">Morning Edition</a></i> has compared the film to a montage of <a href="/wiki/Trope_(literature)" title="Trope (literature)">tropes</a>, with one commentator stating that <i>Avatar</i> was made by mixing a bunch of film scripts in a blender.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257"><span>[</span>257<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gary_Westfahl" title="Gary Westfahl">Gary Westfahl</a> wrote that "the science fiction story that most closely resembles <i>Avatar</i> has to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ursula_Le_Guin" title="Ursula Le Guin">Ursula K. Le Guin's</a> novella "<a href="/wiki/The_Word_for_World_Is_Forest" title="The Word for World Is Forest">The Word for World Is Forest</a>" (1972), another epic about a benevolent race of alien beings who happily inhabit dense forests while living in harmony with nature until they are attacked and slaughtered by invading human soldiers who believe that the only good <a href="/wiki/Gook" title="Gook">gook</a> is a dead gook."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258"><span>[</span>258<span>]</span></a></sup> The science fiction writer and editor <a href="/wiki/Gardner_Dozois" title="Gardner Dozois">Gardner Dozois</a> said that along with the Anderson and Le Guin stories, the "mash-up" included <a href="/wiki/Alan_Dean_Foster" title="Alan Dean Foster">Alan Dean Foster</a>'s 1975 novel, <i><a href="/wiki/Midworld" title="Midworld">Midworld</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259"><span>[</span>259<span>]</span></a></sup> Some sources saw similarities to the artwork of <a href="/wiki/Roger_Dean_(artist)" title="Roger Dean (artist)">Roger Dean</a>, which featured <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fantasy_art" title="Fantasy art">fantastic images</a> of floating rock formations and dragons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-io9dean_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-io9dean-260"><span>[</span>260<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261"><span>[</span>261<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2013, Dean sued Cameron and Fox, claiming that Pandora was inspired by 14 of his images. Dean sought damages of $50m.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262"><span>[</span>262<span>]</span></a></sup> Dean's case was dismissed in 2014, and the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hollywood_Reporter" title="Hollywood Reporter">Hollywood Reporter</a></i> noted that Cameron has won multiple <i>Avatar</i> idea theft cases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263"><span>[</span>263<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Avatar</i> received compliments from filmmakers, with <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> praising it as "the most evocative and amazing science-fiction movie since <i>Star Wars</i>" and others calling it "audacious and awe inspiring", "master class", and "brilliant". Noted art director-turned-filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Roger_Christian_(filmmaker)" title="Roger Christian (filmmaker)">Roger Christian</a> is also a noted fan of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-264"><a href="#cite_note-264"><span>[</span>264<span>]</span></a></sup> On the other hand, <a href="/wiki/Duncan_Jones" title="Duncan Jones">Duncan Jones</a> said: "It's not in my top three James Cameron films. ... [A]t what point in the film did you have any doubt what was going to happen next?".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheBuzz_265-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheBuzz-265"><span>[</span>265<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> ranked <i>Avatar</i> number 3 in their list of "The 10 Greatest Movies of the Millennium (Thus Far)"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266"><span>[</span>266<span>]</span></a></sup> also earning it a spot on the magazine's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time%27s_All-TIME_100_Movies" title="Time's All-TIME 100 Movies">All-TIME 100 list</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267"><span>[</span>267<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> listed <i>Avatar</i> as number 22 on their list of the top 25 Sci-Fi movies of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268"><span>[</span>268<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades <span id="Awards"></span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_Avatar" title="List of accolades received by Avatar">List of accolades received by Avatar</a></div>
<p><i>Avatar</i> won the <a href="/wiki/82nd_Academy_Awards" title="82nd Academy Awards">82nd Academy Awards</a> for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Art_Direction" title="Academy Award for Best Art Direction">Best Art Direction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Cinematography" title="Academy Award for Best Cinematography">Best Cinematography</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects" title="Academy Award for Best Visual Effects">Best Visual Effects</a>, and was nominated for a total of nine, including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Best Picture</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Academy Award for Best Director">Best Director</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-List_of_Academy_Award_nominations_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-List_of_Academy_Award_nominations-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Avatar</i> also won the <a href="/wiki/67th_Golden_Globe_Awards" title="67th Golden Globe Awards">67th Golden Globe Awards</a> for <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Motion_Picture_%E2%80%93_Drama" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Motion Picture – Drama">Best Motion Picture – Drama</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Director">Best Director</a>, and was nominated for two others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-269"><a href="#cite_note-269"><span>[</span>269<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/36th_Saturn_Awards" title="36th Saturn Awards">36th Saturn Awards</a>, <i>Avatar</i> won all ten awards it was nominated for: <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Science_Fiction_Film" title="Saturn Award for Best Science Fiction Film">Best Science Fiction Film</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Actor" title="Saturn Award for Best Actor">Best Actor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Actress" title="Saturn Award for Best Actress">Best Actress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor" title="Saturn Award for Best Supporting Actor">Best Supporting Actor</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actress" title="Saturn Award for Best Supporting Actress">Best Supporting Actress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Saturn Award for Best Director">Best Director</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Writing" title="Saturn Award for Best Writing">Best Writing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Music" title="Saturn Award for Best Music">Best Music</a>, Best Production Design and <a href="/wiki/Saturn_Award_for_Best_Special_Effects" title="Saturn Award for Best Special Effects">Best Special Effects</a>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/New_York_Film_Critics_Online" title="New York Film Critics Online">New York Film Critics Online</a> honored the film with its Best Picture award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-270"><a href="#cite_note-270"><span>[</span>270<span>]</span></a></sup> The film also won the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Critics%27_Choice_Awards" title="Critics' Choice Awards">Critics' Choice Awards</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_Film_Critics_Association" title="Broadcast Film Critics Association">Broadcast Film Critics Association</a> for Best Action Film and several technical categories, out of nine nominations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271"><span>[</span>271<span>]</span></a></sup> It won two of the St. Louis Film Critics awards: Best Visual Effects and Most Original, Innovative or Creative Film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272"><span>[</span>272<span>]</span></a></sup> The film also won the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">British Academy of Film and Television Arts</a> (BAFTA) award for Production Design and Special Visual Effects, and was nominated for seven others, including Best Film and Director.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273"><span>[</span>273<span>]</span></a></sup> The film has received numerous other major awards, nominations and honors.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extended_theatrical_re-release">Extended theatrical re-release</span></h3>
<p>In July 2010, Cameron confirmed that there would be an extended theatrical re-release of the film on <span class="nowrap">August 27</span>, 2010, exclusively in 3D theaters and IMAX 3D.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274"><span>[</span>274<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Avatar: Special Edition</i> includes an additional nine minutes of footage, all of which is <a href="/wiki/Computer_graphics" title="Computer graphics">CG</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarketSaw_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-MarketSaw-275"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup> including an extension of the sex scene<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276"><span>[</span>276<span>]</span></a></sup> and various other scenes that were cut from the original theatrical film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MarketSaw_275-1"><a href="#cite_note-MarketSaw-275"><span>[</span>275<span>]</span></a></sup> This extended re-release resulted in the film's run time approaching the current IMAX platter maximum of 170 minutes, thereby leaving less time for the end credits. Cameron stated that the nine minutes of added scenes cost more than <span class="nowrap">$1 million</span> a minute to produce and finish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bandwagon_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-bandwagon-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> During its 12-week re-release, <i>Avatar: Special Edition</i> grossed an additional $10.74 million in North America and $22.46 million overseas for a worldwide total of $33.2 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boxofficemojo_7-6"><a href="#cite_note-Boxofficemojo-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media <span id="DVD"></span><span id="Video"></span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox_Home_Entertainment" title="20th Century Fox Home Entertainment">20th Century Fox Home Entertainment</a> released the film on DVD and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a> in the US on <span class="nowrap">April 22</span>, 2010<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277"><span>[</span>277<span>]</span></a></sup> and in the UK on <span class="nowrap">April 26</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278"><span>[</span>278<span>]</span></a></sup> The US release was not on a Tuesday as is the norm, but was done to coincide with <a href="/wiki/Earth_Day" title="Earth Day">Earth Day</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279"><span>[</span>279<span>]</span></a></sup> The first DVD and Blu-ray release does not contain any supplemental features other than the theatrical film and the disc menu in favor of and to make space for optimal picture and sound. The release also preserves the film's native 1.78:1 (<a href="/wiki/16:9" title="16:9">16:9</a>) format as Cameron felt that was the best format to watch the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280"><span>[</span>280<span>]</span></a></sup> The Blu-ray disc contains <a href="/wiki/Digital_rights_management" title="Digital rights management">DRM</a> (<a href="/wiki/BD%2B" title="BD+">BD+ 5</a>) which some Blu-ray players might not support without a <a href="/wiki/Firmware" title="Firmware">firmware</a> update.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281"><span>[</span>281<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282"><span>[</span>282<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Avatar</i> set a first-day launch record in the U.S. for Blu-ray sales at 1.5 million units sold, breaking the record previously held by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i> (600,000 units sold). First-day DVD and Blu-ray sales combined were over four million units sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283"><span>[</span>283<span>]</span></a></sup> In its first four days of release, sales of <i>Avatar</i> on Blu-ray reached 2.7 million in the United States and Canada – overtaking <i>The Dark Knight</i> to become the best ever selling Blu-ray release in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284"><span>[</span>284<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285"><span>[</span>285<span>]</span></a></sup> The release later broke the Blu-ray sales record in the UK the following week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286"><span>[</span>286<span>]</span></a></sup> In its first three weeks of release, the film sold a total of <span class="nowrap">19.7 million</span> DVD and Blu-ray discs combined, a new record for sales in that period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-threedisc_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-threedisc-287"><span>[</span>287<span>]</span></a></sup> As of <span class="nowrap">July 18</span>, 2012, DVD sales (not including Blu-ray) totaled over <span class="nowrap">10.5 million</span> units sold with <span class="nowrap">$190,806,055</span> in revenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288"><span>[</span>288<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Avatar</i> retained its record as the top-selling Blu-ray in the US market until January 2015 when Disney's <i><a href="/wiki/Frozen_(2013_film)" title="Frozen (2013 film)">Frozen</a></i> surpassed it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289"><span>[</span>289<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>Avatar</i> Three-Disc Extended Collector's Edition on DVD and Blu-ray was released on <span class="nowrap">November 16</span>, 2010. Three different versions of the film are present on the discs: the original theatrical cut, the special edition cut, and a collector's extended cut<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extendededition_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-extendededition-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> (with the DVD set spreading them on two discs, but the Blu-ray set presenting them on a single disc). The collector's extended cut contains 6 more minutes of footage, thus making it 16 minutes longer than the original theatrical cut. Cameron mentioned, "you can sit down, and in a continuous screening of the film, watch it with the Earth opening". He stated the "Earth opening" is an additional 4<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>2</sub></span> minutes of scenes that were in the film for much of its production but were ultimately cut before the film's theatrical release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290"><span>[</span>290<span>]</span></a></sup> The release also includes an additional 45 minutes of deleted scenes and other extras.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extendededition_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-extendededition-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cameron initially stated that <i>Avatar</i> would be released in 3D around <span class="nowrap">November 2010</span>, but the studio issued a correction: "3-D is in the conceptual stage and <i>Avatar</i> will not be out on 3D Blu-ray in November."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3D_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-3D-291"><span>[</span>291<span>]</span></a></sup> In <span class="nowrap">May 2010</span>, Fox stated that the 3D version would be released some time in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-threedisc_287-1"><a href="#cite_note-threedisc-287"><span>[</span>287<span>]</span></a></sup> It was later revealed that Fox had given <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">Panasonic</a> an exclusive license for the 3D Blu-ray version and only with the purchase of a Panasonic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/3DTV#TV_sets" title="3DTV">3DTV</a>. The length of Panasonic's exclusivity period is stated to last until <span class="nowrap">February 2012</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292"><span>[</span>292<span>]</span></a></sup> On <span class="nowrap">October 2010</span>, Cameron stated that the standalone 3D Blu-ray would be the final version of the film's home release and that it was, "maybe one, two years out".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293"><span>[</span>293<span>]</span></a></sup> On Christmas Eve 2010, <i>Avatar</i> had its 3D television world premiere on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Sky_Broadcasting" title="British Sky Broadcasting">Sky</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294"><span>[</span>294<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295"><span>[</span>295<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296"><span>[</span>296<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On August 13, 2012, Cameron announced on Facebook that <i>Avatar</i> would be released globally on Blu-ray 3D.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-297"><a href="#cite_note-297"><span>[</span>297<span>]</span></a></sup> The Blu-ray 3D version was finally released on October 16, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298"><span>[</span>298<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sequels">Sequels</span></h2>
<p>In 2006, Cameron stated that if <i>Avatar</i> was successful, he hoped to make two <a href="/wiki/Sequel" title="Sequel">sequels</a> to the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carroll2006_299-0"><a href="#cite_note-carroll2006-299"><span>[</span>299<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2010, he said the film's widespread success confirmed that he would.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sequel_300-0"><a href="#cite_note-sequel-300"><span>[</span>300<span>]</span></a></sup> The prospect of sequels was something he planned from the start, going so far as to include certain scenes in the film for future story followups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-carroll2006_299-1"><a href="#cite_note-carroll2006-299"><span>[</span>299<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-movies.yahoo.com_301-0"><a href="#cite_note-movies.yahoo.com-301"><span>[</span>301<span>]</span></a></sup> In <span class="nowrap">August 2010</span>, Cameron stated that he planned to shoot both sequels <a href="/wiki/Back_to_back_film_production" title="Back to back film production">back-to-back</a>. He also mentioned that "presumably, once the novel is nailed down, work will begin in earnest on getting the sequel going."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trilogy_302-0"><a href="#cite_note-trilogy-302"><span>[</span>302<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Cameron stated that they are going to widen the universe while exploring other moons of <a href="/wiki/Fictional_universe_of_Avatar#Astronomy_and_geology" title="Fictional universe of Avatar">Polyphemus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3D_291-1"><a href="#cite_note-3D-291"><span>[</span>291<span>]</span></a></sup> The first sequel will focus on the ocean of Pandora but will also feature more of the rainforest setting from the original movie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Day2010_303-0"><a href="#cite_note-Day2010-303"><span>[</span>303<span>]</span></a></sup> Later in 2010, Cameron announced his intention to capture footage for this sequel at the bottom of the <a href="/wiki/Mariana_Trench" title="Mariana Trench">Mariana Trench</a> using a deepwater submersible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Harlow2010_304-0"><a href="#cite_note-Harlow2010-304"><span>[</span>304<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 2011, Cameron revealed that he was writing second and third films together, but that he was just starting to design the ocean ecosystem of Pandora and the other worlds to be included in the story. The storyline, although continuing the environmental theme of the first film, will not be "strident" since the film will concentrate on entertainment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305"><span>[</span>305<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The sequels will continue to follow the characters of Jake and Neytiri.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306"><span>[</span>306<span>]</span></a></sup> Cameron implied that the humans would return as the antagonists of the story. "I expect that those nasty humans didn't go away forever," he said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307"><span>[</span>307<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sam_Worthington" title="Sam Worthington">Sam Worthington</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zoe_Saldana" title="Zoe Saldana">Zoe Saldana</a> have signed on to reprise their roles in the sequels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-movies.yahoo.com_301-1"><a href="#cite_note-movies.yahoo.com-301"><span>[</span>301<span>]</span></a></sup> In <span class="nowrap">February 2010</span>, Cameron confirmed that <a href="/wiki/Sigourney_Weaver" title="Sigourney Weaver">Sigourney Weaver</a>, who played Dr. Grace Augustine, will also be appearing in <i>Avatar 2</i>, stating that "no one ever dies in science fiction".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308"><span>[</span>308<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Lang" title="Stephen Lang">Stephen Lang</a> is also expected to return despite the demise of his character, Colonel Miles Quaritch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309"><span>[</span>309<span>]</span></a></sup> The sequels, to be produced by Cameron's own <a href="/wiki/Lightstorm_Entertainment" title="Lightstorm Entertainment">Lightstorm Entertainment</a> in partnership with <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a>, were originally scheduled to be released in <span class="nowrap">December 2014</span> and <span class="nowrap">December 2015</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sequels2_310-0"><a href="#cite_note-sequels2-310"><span>[</span>310<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, Cameron stated his intention to film the two <i>Avatar</i> sequels at a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_Frame_Rate_3D" title="High Frame Rate 3D">higher frame rate</a> than the industry standard 24 frames per second, in order to add a heightened sense of reality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311"><span>[</span>311<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312"><span>[</span>312<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2012, Cameron first mentioned a third sequel, saying that he was "making <i>Avatar 2</i>, <i>Avatar 3</i>, maybe <i>Avatar 4</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313"><span>[</span>313<span>]</span></a></sup> In June 2012, Sigourney Weaver revealed that the three sequels would shoot simultaneously, but she was not sure how long shooting for the movies was expected to take.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314"><span>[</span>314<span>]</span></a></sup> In September 2012, Cameron told MTV the concept for the fourth movie. It would be a <a href="/wiki/Prequel" title="Prequel">prequel</a>, set 35 years before the events of the first film, that deals with the early colonization of Pandora.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315"><span>[</span>315<span>]</span></a></sup> That same month, while promoting the 3D Blu-ray release of <i>Titanic</i>, he stated that the scripts for the second and third <i>Avatar</i> parts are still being written, with both being "separate stories that have an overall arc inclusive of the first film" and the second having a clear conclusion instead of a <a href="/wiki/Cliffhanger" title="Cliffhanger">cliffhanger</a> to the third film. Cameron expected to start pre-production in January 2013 and release <i>Avatar 2</i> in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316"><span>[</span>316<span>]</span></a></sup> In August 2013, it was confirmed that there would be three sequels. Screenwriters were also announced: <a href="/wiki/Josh_Friedman" title="Josh Friedman">Josh Friedman</a> for the first, <a href="/wiki/Rick_Jaffa_and_Amanda_Silver" title="Rick Jaffa and Amanda Silver">Rick Jaffa and Amanda Silver</a> for the second, and <a href="/wiki/Shane_Salerno" title="Shane Salerno">Shane Salerno</a> for the third. Production was re-scheduled for 2014 with the films to be released in December 2016, 2017, and 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317"><span>[</span>317<span>]</span></a></sup> In October 2013 Worthington stated that filming for the first sequel was expected to begin in October 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318"><span>[</span>318<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2013, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Steven_Gould" title="Steven Gould">Steven Gould</a> had been engaged to write four novels based on the films.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319"><span>[</span>319<span>]</span></a></sup> In December 2013, Cameron announced that the three sequels would be filmed in New Zealand. He stated that performance capture would take place in the second half of 2014 and that as much post-production will be done in New Zealand as possible. A deal made with the <a href="/wiki/Fifth_National_Government_of_New_Zealand" title="Fifth National Government of New Zealand">New Zealand government</a> requires that at least one world premiere be held in Wellington and that at least <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_dollar" title="New Zealand dollar">NZ$</a>500 million (approximately US$410 million at December 2013 exchange rates) would be spent on production activity in New Zealand, including live-action filming and visuals effects by Weta Workshop. In tandem with this announcement, the New Zealand government announced it would raise its baseline tax rebate for filmmaking from 15% to 20%, with 25% available to international productions in some cases and 40% for New Zealand productions (as defined by section 18 of the <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Film_Commission" title="New Zealand Film Commission">New Zealand Film Commission</a> Act 1978).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NZgovt1_320-0"><a href="#cite_note-NZgovt1-320"><span>[</span>320<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321"><span>[</span>321<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2014 Cameron revealed that he was currently working on the three scripts for the sequels, which he expected to be finished within six weeks (late May). He confirmed that all three sequels would be into production simultaneously, slated for December 2016 to 2018 releases.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-322"><a href="#cite_note-322"><span>[</span>322<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-323"><a href="#cite_note-323"><span>[</span>323<span>]</span></a></sup> He also confirmed that Sigourney Weaver would be featured in all three sequels and that her character Grace Augustine would be alive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324"><span>[</span>324<span>]</span></a></sup> As of November 2014, Pre-production had begun.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325"><span>[</span>325<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Discussing the writing process, Cameron stated that although Friedman, Jaffa and Silver, and Salerno are each co-writing one sequel with him, they at first worked all together for several months on all three scripts with him, without knowing which movie he was going to assign to each: "We whiteboarded out every scene in every film together, and I didn’t assign each writer which film they were going to work on until the last day. I knew if I assigned them their scripts ahead of time, they’d tune out every time we were talking about the other movie."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326"><span>[</span>326<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327"><span>[</span>327<span>]</span></a></sup> "We sat in the writing room for five months, eight hours a day, and we worked out every beat of the story across all three films so it all connects as one, sort of, three-film saga."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328"><span>[</span>328<span>]</span></a></sup> On January 14, 2015, the scheduled release dates for the sequels were each delayed by a year, with the first sequel expected to be released in December 2017; Cameron called the writing process "a complex job".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329"><span>[</span>329<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330"><a href="#cite_note-330"><span>[</span>330<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

Abrams. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-8109-9706-6" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-8109-9706-6">978-0-8109-9706-6</a>. <a href="/wiki/OCLC" title="OCLC">OCLC</a> <a class="external text" href="//www.worldcat.org/oclc/555654027" rel="nofollow">555654027</a>.</span><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAvatar+%282009+film%29&amp;rft.au=Duncan%2C+Jody&amp;rft.aufirst=Jody&amp;rft.au=Fitzpatrick%2C+Lisa&amp;rft.aulast=Duncan&amp;rft.btitle=The+Making+of+Avatar&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=info%3Aoclcnum%2F555654027&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-8109-9706-6&amp;rft.place=New+York&amp;rft.pub=Harry+N.+Abrams&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>

London: Punked Books. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-9533172-5-7" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-9533172-5-7">978-0-9533172-5-7</a>.</span><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AAvatar+%282009+film%29&amp;rft.aufirst=Kevin+Patrick&amp;rft.aulast=Mahoney&amp;rft.au=Mahoney%2C+Kevin+Patrick&amp;rft.btitle=The+Ultimate+Fan%27s+Guide+to+Avatar%2C+James+Cameron%27s+Epic+Movie+%28Unauthorized%29&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.ca%2Fbooks%3Fid%3D-ZWhqcOYkwYC&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-9533172-5-7&amp;rft.place=London&amp;rft.pub=Punked+Books&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>
